The Duality of the Penalty for a Muhrim Killing Game: Kaffarah and Badal
Explaining the dual nature and the rule on multiplicity with intention to leave ihram

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the dual nature of the penalty (jaza') for a muhrim who kills game, state the Hanafi ruling on multiplicity when killing with intent to leave ihram, and evaluate the analogy with muhsar.

Core Idea
The penalty for a muhrim killing game is both expiation (kaffarah) and indemnity (badal).

This lesson explores a distinctive Hanafi position on the penalty (jaza') for a muhrim who kills game. The text from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq establishes that the penalty is not merely an expiation but also a compensation. This duality affects rulings on multiplicity and intention, leading to a nuanced position that differs from other schools.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What is the act being ruled upon (killing game while in ihram) and what is the general hukm? The passage states the penalty is wajib, consisting of options: sacrifice, feeding, or fasting.
The act is killing game, which is a prohibited act (mahzur) of ihram.
2
Locate the dalil
What proof does the author cite for the dual nature? The verse (5:95) uses the word 'kaffarah', but also the requirement of equivalence (mumathalah) indicates a compensatory aspect.
The verse: 'or a kaffarah of feeding the poor' (أو كفارة طعام مساكين).
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
How does the dalil prove the dual nature? The word 'kaffarah' directly shows expiation; the consideration of value (muttaqawwim) and equivalency shows that the penalty is also a badal.
The author says: 'أما كونه بدلاً فلوجود سببه وهو إتلاف صيد متقوم' (as for it being an indemnity, due to the destruction of valuable game).
4
Note the ikhtilaf
What is the dispute regarding multiplicity with intention to leave ihram? Some scholars (unnamed) argue the analogy with muhsar is invalid because the muhsar's exit is legitimate, while the muhrim's intention is sinful and ineffective.
The objection is based on the difference in legitimacy of the action.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi tarjih
How does the Hanafi school resolve the dispute? The relied-upon position (from al-Asl and al-Mabsut) is that one dam suffices, regardless of the intention's validity. The existence or non-existence of the intention is irrelevant; the act triggers the penalty.
This ruling is from the core texts (zahir al-riwayah), so it is authoritative despite the logical objection.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الحج فصل إن قتل محرم صيداً وذبحه أن بلغت هدياً أو طعاماً وتصدق به كالفطرة أو صام عن طعام كل مسكين يوماً مسلم من حديث أبي قتادة هل أنتم ، ولا شك أن إعارة السكين إعانة عليه. ثم اعلم أن هذا الجزاء كفارة وبدل عندنا، أما كونه كفارة فلوجود سببها وهو الجناية على الإحرام بارتكاب محظور إحرامه ولهذا قال ﴿أو كفارة طعام مساكين﴾ [المائدة: ٩٥] وأما كونه بدلاً فلوجود سببه وهو إتلاف صيد متقوم ولهذا اعتبرت المماثلة بين المقتول والجزاء، ولهذا ذكر المصنف آخر الباب أنه لو اجتمع محرمان في قتل صيد تعدد الجزاء لأن الواجب كفارة في حق الجاني وجب جزاء على فعله وفعل كل واحد جناية على حدة بخلاف الحلالين كما سيأتي. ثم اعلم أيضاً أن الجزاء بتعدد المقتول إلا إذا قصد به التحلل ورفض إحرامه كما صرح به في الأصل فقال : اصطاد المحرم صيداً كثيراً على قصد الإحلال والرفض لإحرامه فعليه لذلك لأنه قاصد إلى تعجيل الإحلال إلى الجناية على الإحرام وتعجيل الإحلال يوجب دماً واحداً كما في المحصر . كذا في المبسوط . وقد يقال : لا يصح القياس لما أن تعجيل الإحلال في المحصر مشروع بخلافه هنا ولهذا كان قصده باطلاً ولا يرتفض به الإحرام فوجوده وعدمه سواء .
Book of Hajj, Chapter: If a muhrim kills game and slaughters it, that it may reach as a sacrificial animal or food, and he gives it in charity like the charity of fitr, or he fasts for the food of each poor person a day. Muslim from the hadith of Abu Qatadah: 'Are you...' There is no doubt that lending a knife is assisting in it. Then know that this penalty is both kaffarah and indemnity according to us. As for it being kaffarah, due to the existence of its cause, which is the offense against ihram by committing a prohibited act of ihram, and for this He said: 'or a kaffarah of feeding the poor' (5:95). As for it being an indemnity, due to the existence of its cause, which is the destruction of a valuable game, and for this equivalency between the killed and the penalty is considered. And for this the author mentioned at the end of the chapter that if two muhrims are joined in killing a game, the penalty multiplies, because the obligation is a kaffarah on the part of the offender, and a penalty is due for his action, and each action is a separate offense, unlike the case of two non-muhrims as will come. Then also know that the penalty multiplies with the multiplicity of the killed game, unless he intended by it to exit ihram and abandon his ihram, as stated in al-Asl: He said: 'A muhrim who catches many game with the intention of exiting and abandoning his ihram, on him is one dam for that, because he intends to hasten ihram's ending over the offense against ihram, and hastening ihram's ending necessitates one dam, as in the case of a muhsar.' Thus in al-Mabsut. It may be said: The analogy is not valid because hastening ihram's ending in a muhsar is legitimate, unlike here, and for this his intention is void and ihram is not abandoned by it, so its existence and non-existence are equal.
Source pages p. 51

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq opens the chapter on the penalty for a muhrim who kills game. The author first establishes that the penalty (jaza') has a dual nature: it is both a kaffarah (expiation) for violating the sanctity of ihram and a badal (indemnity/compensation) for the destroyed game. The kaffarah aspect is based on the verse (5:95) 'or a kaffarah of feeding the poor,' while the badal aspect is based on the destruction of a valuable (muttaqawwim) animal, hence the requirement of equivalence (mumathalah) between the killed animal and the penalty. The author then discusses a rule: if two muhrims jointly kill one game, the penalty is multiplied by the number of offenders because each committed a separate offense. But if a single muhrim kills multiple games with the specific intention of leaving ihram (by committing the offense), then only one dam is due because the underlying intention is to hasten ihram's end, similar to a muhsar (one prevented from completing Hajj). Some objected that this analogy is flawed because intended hastening of ihram in a muhsar is legitimate, while here the intention is sinful and ineffective; however, the ruling of one dam stands regardless as per al-Mabsut.

Key Terms
جزاء (jaza'): The penalty or recompense for killing game while in ihram, which is both kaffarah (expiation) and badal (indemnity).
كفارة (kaffarah): Expiation for a sin or error, specifically for violating the prohibition of hunting in ihram.
بدل (badal): Indemnity or compensation for a destroyed valuable property, here the game animal.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the nature of the penalty (jaza') for a muhrim who kills game?
A) It is purely a kaffarah (expiation) for violating ihram.
B) It is purely a badal (indemnity) for the destroyed game.
C) It is both a kaffarah and a badal.
D) It is a fine paid to the state.

Key Takeaway
The penalty (jaza') for a muhrim killing game is both a kaffarah (expiation) and a badal (indemnity); when multiple game are killed with intent to leave ihram, only one dam is due.

The Ruling for Killing Game in Ihram: Valuation and Options
Ruling and its Quranic proof

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling for the penalty of killing game in ihram and identify the Quranic verse that serves as its primary proof.

Core Idea
The penalty is the value estimated by two just men, derived from Quran 5:95.

In this passage, the author clarifies the practical implementation of the penalty for a muhrim who kills game. The ruling is tied directly to the Quranic text but with an important nuance: the penalty applies whether the killing was intentional or forgetful, as it is not purely expiatory.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What is the penalty for killing game? It is the value estimated by two just men, then three options: sacrifice, feed the poor, or fast.
2
Locate the dalil
The verse 5:95 is cited. Understand that the verse mentions 'the like' (muthl) which is interpreted as value.
The verse is the primary proof.
3
Analyze the wajh al-dalalah
How does the word 'muthl' lead to value? The Hanafi interpretation takes it as like in meaning, not form.
This step foreshadows the inter-madhhab dispute.
4
Note the generality of the ruling
The author generalizes the ruling to both intentional and forgetful acts, unlike the verse's wording.
The reason: the penalty is not purely kaffarah but also compensatory.
5
Understand the three options
The value can be used for a sacrificial animal, food charity, or fasting. The choice depends on the amount.
The conversion ratio is based on the value.

قوله : (وهو قيمة الصيد بتقويم عدلين في مقتله أو أقرب موضع منه فيشتري بها هدياً وذبحه إن بلغت هدياً أو طعاماً وتصدق به كالفطرة أو صام عن طعام كل مسكين يوماً) أي الحزاء ما ذكر لقوله تعالى ﴿ومن قتله منكم متعمداً فجزاء مثل ما قتل من النعم يحكم به ذوا عدل منكم هديا بالغ الكعبة أو كفارة طعام مساكين أو عدل ذلك صياما ليذوق وبال أمره﴾ [المائدة : ٩٥] اطلق المصنف ولم يقيد بالعمد كما في الآية لأنه لا فرق بين الناسي والعامد كإتلاف الأمول لأن هذا الجزاء ليس كفارة محضة كما قدمنا والتقييد به في الآية لأجل الوعيد المذكور في آخرها لا لوجوب الجزاء، لأن الآية نزلت في حق من تعدى كما ذكره القاضي البيضاوي. وأشار بذكر القيمة فقط إلى أنها المراد بالمثل في الآية وهو المثل معنى المثل صورة ومعنى، وإنما لم يعمل بالكامل كما قال محمد والشافعي فإنهما أوجبا النظير فيما لا نظير له لأن المعهود في الشرع في القيميات المثل معنى فإنه لو أتلف بقرة لإنسان مثلاً لا يلزمه بقرة مثلها اتفاقاً لأن المثل معنى مراد بالإجماع فيما لا نظير له وهو مجاز فلا يراد المعنى الحقيقي وهو المثل صورة ومعنى لعدم جواز الجمع بين الحقيقة والمجاز، وكذلك في قوله تعالى ﴿فاعتدوا عليه بمثل ما اعتدى عليكم﴾ [البقرة : ۱۹٤] أريد المثل معنى وهو القيمة، وأما رد العين فثابت بالسنة أو لما في حملنا على المثل معنى من التعميم لشموله ماله نظير له وما لا نظير له، وإذا حمل على المثل الكامل كانت الآية قاصرة على ماله نظير. وعلى هذا فكلمة من النعم بيان لـ«ما» وهو المقتول لا للمثل . والنعم كما يطلق على الأهلي يطلق على الوحشي كما قاله أبو عبيده والأصمعي وأراد بقيمة الصيد قيمة لحمه. قال الكرماني في مناسكه : يقوم الصيد لحماً عندنا وقال زفر يجب قيمته بالغة ما بلغت. وفائدة الخلاف لو قتل بازياً معلماً فعندنا تجب قيمته لحماً، وعنده تجب قيمته معلماً. وفي الاختيار : وإذا كان المراد من الجزاء القيمة يقوم العد لأن اللحم لا الحيوان والمراد أنه يقوم من حيث الذات لا من حيث الصفة لأنها أمر عارض ولو كانت الصفة بأمر خلقي كما إذا كان طيراً يصوت فازدادت قيمته لذلك ففي اعتبار ذلك في الجزاء روايتان ورجح في البدائع اعتبارها بخلاف ما إذا أتلف شيئاً مملوكاً فإن القيمة تعتبر من حيث الذات والصفات إلا إذا كان الوصف لمحرم من اللهو كقيمة الديك لنقاره والكبش لنطاحه فإنها لا إهدار ما كان بصنع العباد. وأراد بالعدل من له معرفة وبصارة بقيمة الصيد لا العدل في باب الشهادة وقيد بالعدلين لأن العدل الواحد لا يكفي لظاهر
His saying: (And it is the value of the game by the valuation of two just men at the place where it was killed or the nearest place to it; then he buys with it a sacrificial animal and slaughters it if it suffices for a sacrificial animal, or food and gives it in charity like fitr, or he fasts for the food of each poor person a day.) That is, the penalty is what is mentioned due to His saying, the Exalted: 'And whoever kills it among you intentionally, then the penalty is the like of what he killed from cattle, judged by two just men among you, a sacrificial animal reaching the Ka'bah, or a kaffarah of feeding the poor, or the equivalent of that in fasting, that he may taste the consequence of his deed' (5:95). The author generalized and did not restrict to intentional as in the verse because there is no difference between the forgetful and the intentional, like the destruction of property, because this penalty is not purely kaffarah as we presented earlier. The restriction in the verse is for the threat mentioned at its end, not for the obligation of the penalty, because the verse was revealed concerning the transgressor, as stated by al-Qadi al-Baydawi. He indicated by mentioning only the value that it is what is meant by 'the like' (muthl) in the verse, and it is the like in meaning, not in form and meaning. And they did not act according to the complete like, as Muhammad and al-Shafi'i said, for they obligated the equivalent in what has no equivalent, because the customary in the Shari'ah concerning things valued by price (qimiyyat) is the like in meaning. For example, if someone destroys a cow belonging to another, he is not obliged to a cow like it by agreement, because the like in meaning is intended by consensus for what has no equivalent, and it is a metaphor, so the real meaning (like in form and meaning) is not intended due to the impossibility of combining the real and the metaphorical. Similarly, in His saying 'So aggress against him in the like of what he aggressed against you' (2:194), what is meant is the like in meaning, i.e., the value. As for returning the actual object, it is proven by the sunnah. Or because in our interpretation of 'like' as the like in meaning, there is generality, including what has an equivalent and what has no equivalent. If it were interpreted as the complete like, the verse would be restricted to what has an equivalent. On this basis, the phrase 'from cattle' is a clarification of 'what' (the killed animal), not of 'the like'. And the word 'na'am' (cattle) is applied to domesticated and wild animals as said by Abu Ubaidah and al-Asma'i. By 'value of the game' is meant the value of its meat. Al-Kirmani said in his Manasik: 'The game is valued in meat according to us.' Zufar said: 'Its value must be paid whatever it reaches.' The benefit of the difference is if one kills a trained falcon: according to us, its value in meat is due; according to him, its value as trained. In al-Ikhtiyar: 'When the intended meaning of the penalty is the value, the two just men evaluate the meat, not the animal.' The intended meaning is that it is valued from the aspect of the essence, not from the aspect of quality, because quality is an accidental attribute. Even if the quality is a natural attribute, such as a bird that sings, thus increasing its value, there are two narrations concerning considering that in the penalty. In al-Bada'i', considering it is preferred, unlike if one destroys owned property, where value is considered from the aspect of essence and qualities except if the description is for a prohibited matter of play, such as the value of a rooster for its crowing or a ram for its butting, for these are not considered, like the value of a singing slave girl. They do not mean that it is valued after it is killed; rather it is valued while alive with respect to its essence, as evidenced by the fact that the meat of an inedible animal cannot be valued after killing because it has no value; rather it is valued with respect to its skin and being a live game that benefits from. And they do not intend to completely disregard the attribute of being game, because they agreed that if one kills a beautiful, handsome game with increased value, its value for that attribute is due, as if one kills a ringed dove or a collared turtledove, as in al-Bada'i'. They only intend to disregard what is due to human craftsmanship. By 'just men' is meant one who has knowledge and insight regarding the value of the game, not the just in testimony. And it is restricted to two just men because a single just man is not sufficient, due to the apparent.
Source pages p. 51

Commentary
This passage is a detailed explanation of the matn regarding the valuation of the game and the options for the penalty. The author begins by quoting the Quranic verse (5:95) which explicitly mentions the penalty as 'the like of what he killed from cattle.' The commentary then clarifies that the valuation is based on the value (qimah) of the game, not on a physical 'like' (muthl) in form and species. This is because the Hanafi school interprets 'muthl' in the verse as 'like in meaning' (i.e., monetary value) rather than 'like in form' (identical animal). This is contrasted with the positions of Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani and Imam al-Shafi'i, who require a physical equivalent when possible. The Hanafi view is that the penalty is valued by two just (adil) men who assess the market value of the game at the place of killing or nearest location. The value is then used to purchase a sacrificial animal (if sufficient) or food given in charity (like fitr), or the muhrim may fast one day for each poor person's portion. The valuation is of the meat value (not the live animal) according to the Hanafi school, except that natural attributes like beauty or song may be considered if they increase value, but not attributes from human training (e.g., a trained falcon's training value is not included). The two just men must be knowledgeable about game values, not necessarily just in legal testimony. One just man is insufficient. This ruling applies whether the killing was intentional or forgetful, as the penalty is not purely kaffarah (expiation) but also a badal (indemnity).

Key Terms
مثل (muthl): In this context, 'like' but interpreted by Hanafis as 'like in meaning' (value), not 'like in form' (identical animal).
قيمة (qimah): Monetary value or price: the basis for the penalty according to Hanafis; the game is valued as meat (lahan) by two just men.
عدلين (adlayn): Two just men who have knowledge of game values; they are expert evaluators, not necessarily the same as witnesses of testimony.

Key Terms from Source Passage

The penalty for killing game is the monetary value estimated by two just men, not a physical like.

The Hanafi Interpretation of 'Muthl' and the Dispute with Shafi'i
Interpretation of 'muthl' and inter-madhhab dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why Hanafis interpret 'muthl' as value in the penalty verse and contrast this with the Shafi'i position, and identify the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf).

Core Idea
Muthl means like in meaning (value) not in form; this follows the Hanafi principle for qimiyyat.

This passage delves into the linguistic and legal reasoning behind the Hanafi interpretation of the key term 'muthl' in the penalty verse. The author defends the school's position against those who require a physical equivalent, using analogies from property law and other Quranic verses.

Guided Path
1
Understand the Hanafi position on 'muthl'
The Hanafi school interprets 'muthl' as monetary value, not a physical like.
This is based on the general principle for qimiyyat.
2
Examine the Hanafi evidence
The author cites the retaliation verse (2:194) and the consensus on property destruction to support value interpretation.
3
Identify the opposing view
Muhammad al-Shaybani and al-Shafi'i require a physical equivalent when possible.
4
Evaluate the Hanafi response
The response argues that a literal like is impossible for many games and the custom of Shari'ah is to use value.
Also the phrase 'from cattle' clarifies the killed animal, not the like.
5
Derive the thamarah al-khilaf
For a trained falcon, Hanafis value meat only; Shafi'is value the trained bird. This practical difference illustrates the consequence.

قوله : (وهو قيمة الصيد بتقويم عدلين في مقتله أو أقرب موضع منه فيشتري بها هدياً وذبحه إن بلغت هدياً أو طعاماً وتصدق به كالفطرة أو صام عن طعام كل مسكين يوماً) أي الحزاء ما ذكر لقوله تعالى ﴿ومن قتله منكم متعمداً فجزاء مثل ما قتل من النعم يحكم به ذوا عدل منكم هديا بالغ الكعبة أو كفارة طعام مساكين أو عدل ذلك صياما ليذوق وبال أمره﴾ [المائدة : ٩٥] اطلق المصنف ولم يقيد بالعمد كما في الآية لأنه لا فرق بين الناسي والعامد كإتلاف الأمول لأن هذا الجزاء ليس كفارة محضة كما قدمنا والتقييد به في الآية لأجل الوعيد المذكور في آخرها لا لوجوب الجزاء، لأن الآية نزلت في حق من تعدى كما ذكره القاضي البيضاوي. وأشار بذكر القيمة فقط إلى أنها المراد بالمثل في الآية وهو المثل معنى المثل صورة ومعنى، وإنما لم يعمل بالكامل كما قال محمد والشافعي فإنهما أوجبا النظير فيما لا نظير له لأن المعهود في الشرع في القيميات المثل معنى فإنه لو أتلف بقرة لإنسان مثلاً لا يلزمه بقرة مثلها اتفاقاً لأن المثل معنى مراد بالإجماع فيما لا نظير له وهو مجاز فلا يراد المعنى الحقيقي وهو المثل صورة ومعنى لعدم جواز الجمع بين الحقيقة والمجاز، وكذلك في قوله تعالى ﴿فاعتدوا عليه بمثل ما اعتدى عليكم﴾ [البقرة : ۱۹٤] أريد المثل معنى وهو القيمة، وأما رد العين فثابت بالسنة أو لما في حملنا على المثل معنى من التعميم لشموله ماله نظير له وما لا نظير له، وإذا حمل على المثل الكامل كانت الآية قاصرة على ماله نظير. وعلى هذا فكلمة من النعم بيان لـ«ما» وهو المقتول لا للمثل . والنعم كما يطلق على الأهلي يطلق على الوحشي كما قاله أبو عبيده والأصمعي وأراد بقيمة الصيد قيمة لحمه. قال الكرماني في مناسكه : يقوم الصيد لحماً عندنا وقال زفر يجب قيمته بالغة ما بلغت. وفائدة الخلاف لو قتل بازياً معلماً فعندنا تجب قيمته لحماً، وعنده تجب قيمته معلماً. وفي الاختيار : وإذا كان المراد من الجزاء القيمة يقوم العد لأن اللحم لا الحيوان والمراد أنه يقوم من حيث الذات لا من حيث الصفة لأنها أمر عارض ولو كانت الصفة بأمر خلقي كما إذا كان طيراً يصوت فازدادت قيمته لذلك ففي اعتبار ذلك في الجزاء روايتان ورجح في البدائع اعتبارها بخلاف ما إذا أتلف شيئاً مملوكاً فإن القيمة تعتبر من حيث الذات والصفات إلا إذا كان الوصف لمحرم من اللهو كقيمة الديك لنقاره والكبش لنطاحه فإنها لا تعتبر كالجارية المغنية . وليس مرادهم انه يقوم بعد قتله وإنما يقوم وهو حي باعتبار ذاته بدليل أن مالا يؤكل لحمه لا أن يقوم لحمه يصح بعد قتله إذ ليس له قيمة وإنما يقوم باعتبار جلده وكونه صيداً حياً ينتفع به، وليس مرادهم إهدار صفة الصيد بالكلية لما أنهم اتفقوا على أنه لو قتل صيداً حسناً مليحاً له زيادة قيمة تجب قيمته على تلك الصفة كما لو قتل حمامة مطوقة أو فاختة مطوقة كما به في البدائع. وإنما المراد إهدار ما كان بصنع العباد. وأراد بالعدل من له معرفة وبصارة بقيمة الصيد لا العدل في باب الشهادة وقيد بالعدلين لأن العدل الواحد لا يكفي لظاهر
His saying: (And it is the value of the game by the valuation of two just men at the place where it was killed or the nearest place to it; then he buys with it a sacrificial animal and slaughters it if it suffices for a sacrificial animal, or food and gives it in charity like fitr, or he fasts for the food of each poor person a day.) That is, the penalty is what is mentioned due to His saying, the Exalted: 'And whoever kills it among you intentionally, then the penalty is the like of what he killed from cattle, judged by two just men among you, a sacrificial animal reaching the Ka'bah, or a kaffarah of feeding the poor, or the equivalent of that in fasting, that he may taste the consequence of his deed' (5:95). The author generalized and did not restrict to intentional as in the verse because there is no difference between the forgetful and the intentional, like the destruction of property, because this penalty is not purely kaffarah as we presented earlier. The restriction in the verse is for the threat mentioned at its end, not for the obligation of the penalty, because the verse was revealed concerning the transgressor, as stated by al-Qadi al-Baydawi. He indicated by mentioning only the value that it is what is meant by 'the like' (muthl) in the verse, and it is the like in meaning, not in form and meaning. And they did not act according to the complete like, as Muhammad and al-Shafi'i said, for they obligated the equivalent in what has no equivalent, because the customary in the Shari'ah concerning things valued by price (qimiyyat) is the like in meaning. For example, if someone destroys a cow belonging to another, he is not obliged to a cow like it by agreement, because the like in meaning is intended by consensus for what has no equivalent, and it is a metaphor, so the real meaning (like in form and meaning) is not intended due to the impossibility of combining the real and the metaphorical. Similarly, in His saying 'So aggress against him in the like of what he aggressed against you' (2:194), what is meant is the like in meaning, i.e., the value. As for returning the actual object, it is proven by the sunnah. Or because in our interpretation of 'like' as the like in meaning, there is generality, including what has an equivalent and what has no equivalent. If it were interpreted as the complete like, the verse would be restricted to what has an equivalent. On this basis, the phrase 'from cattle' is a clarification of 'what' (the killed animal), not of 'the like'. And the word 'na'am' (cattle) is applied to domesticated and wild animals as said by Abu Ubaidah and al-Asma'i. By 'value of the game' is meant the value of its meat. Al-Kirmani said in his Manasik: 'The game is valued in meat according to us.' Zufar said: 'Its value must be paid whatever it reaches.' The benefit of the difference is if one kills a trained falcon: according to us, its value in meat is due; according to him, its value as trained. In al-Ikhtiyar: 'When the intended meaning of the penalty is the value, the two just men evaluate the meat, not the animal.' The intended meaning is that it is valued from the aspect of the essence, not from the aspect of quality, because quality is an accidental attribute. Even if the quality is a natural attribute, such as a bird that sings, thus increasing its value, there are two narrations concerning considering that in the penalty. In al-Bada'i', considering it is preferred, unlike if one destroys owned property, where value is considered from the aspect of essence and qualities except if the description is for a prohibited matter of play, such as the value of a rooster for its crowing or a ram for its butting, for these are not considered, like the value of a singing slave girl. They do not mean that it is valued after it is killed; rather it is valued while alive with respect to its essence, as evidenced by the fact that the meat of an inedible animal cannot be valued after killing because it has no value; rather it is valued with respect to its skin and being a live game that benefits from. And they do not intend to completely disregard the attribute of being game, because they agreed that if one kills a beautiful, handsome game with increased value, its value for that attribute is due, as if one kills a ringed dove or a collared turtledove, as in al-Bada'i'. They only intend to disregard what is due to human craftsmanship. By 'just men' is meant one who has knowledge and insight regarding the value of the game, not the just in testimony. And it is restricted to two just men because a single just man is not sufficient, due to the apparent.
Source pages p. 51

Commentary
This passage is a detailed explanation of the matn regarding the valuation of the game and the options for the penalty. The author begins by quoting the Quranic verse (5:95) which explicitly mentions the penalty as 'the like of what he killed from cattle.' The commentary then clarifies that the valuation is based on the value (qimah) of the game, not on a physical 'like' (muthl) in form and species. This is because the Hanafi school interprets 'muthl' in the verse as 'like in meaning' (i.e., monetary value) rather than 'like in form' (identical animal). This is contrasted with the positions of Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani and Imam al-Shafi'i, who require a physical equivalent when possible. The Hanafi view is that the penalty is valued by two just (adil) men who assess the market value of the game at the place of killing or nearest location. The value is then used to purchase a sacrificial animal (if sufficient) or food given in charity (like fitr), or the muhrim may fast one day for each poor person's portion. The valuation is of the meat value (not the live animal) according to the Hanafi school, except that natural attributes like beauty or song may be considered if they increase value, but not attributes from human training (e.g., a trained falcon's training value is not included). The two just men must be knowledgeable about game values, not necessarily just in legal testimony. One just man is insufficient. This ruling applies whether the killing was intentional or forgetful, as the penalty is not purely kaffarah (expiation) but also a badal (indemnity).

Key Terms
مثل (muthl): In this context, 'like' but interpreted by Hanafis as 'like in meaning' (value), not 'like in form' (identical animal).
قيمة (qimah): Monetary value or price: the basis for the penalty according to Hanafis; the game is valued as meat (lahan) by two just men.
عدلين (adlayn): Two just men who have knowledge of game values; they are expert evaluators, not necessarily the same as witnesses of testimony.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway

Rulings on Valuation and Expiation for a Muhrim Who Kills Game
Expansion of a madhhab dispute on expiation choice

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on who chooses the expiation after killing game in ihram and explain the grammatical and analogical proofs, distinguishing the killer's right from the arbiters' role.

Core Idea
The killer, not the arbiters, chooses among sacrifice, feeding, or fasting.

When a muhrim kills game, the expiation involves valuation by two just witnesses. But who decides which form of expiation? This lesson unpacks a key inter-madhhab dispute: the Hanafi school holds that the choice belongs to the killer, while Muhammad al-Shaybani and al-Shafi'i assign it to the arbiters. We'll trace the proofs from Quranic grammar, analogy with oath expiation, and practical consequences.

Guided Path
1
Identify the dispute: Who chooses the expiation?
The passage contrasts two views: Hanafis say the killer chooses; Muhammad and al-Shafi'i say the two arbiters choose. Articulate the exact point of disagreement.
The choice is among three options: sacrificial animal (هدي), feeding the poor (إطعام), or fasting (صيام).
2
Examine the Hanafi proof from Quranic grammar
The passage argues that the words 'أو كفارة أو عدل' (or expiation or justice) are in the nominative case (مرفوع) as adjuncts of 'جزاء' (penalty), not accusative (منصوب) as adjuncts of 'هدياً' (sacrificial animal). This shows the choice is with the killer, not the arbiters.
The nominative case indicates these are independent options appositionally linked to 'جزاء'.
3
Consider the analogy with oath expiation
The passage likens this to expiation of an oath (كفارة اليمين), where the one who broke the oath chooses among feeding, clothing, or fasting. Since both are expiations, the same leniency applies: the obligated person chooses.
This is a qiyas (analogy) based on shared illa: providing ease for the obligee.
4
Analyze the opposing proof and Hanafi response
The opposing view (Muhammad and al-Shafi'i) holds that the arbiters choose, based on the apparent meaning of the verse that they 'judge' (يحكم). The Hanafi response: the arbiters only evaluate the value; the verse does not give them choice. The nominative reading precludes their authority over the expiation type.
The thamarah al-khilaf: if the arbiters choose, they might impose a costlier option; if the killer chooses, he can select the cheapest.
5
Determine the mufta bihi position
The Hanafi school relies on the view that the killer chooses after the arbiters set the value. This is the position in al-Hidayah and preferred by later authorities (mufta bihi).
The killer's choice must be exercised after knowing the value; the arbiters' role is purely evaluative.

Source Text

كتاب الحج/ فصل إن قتل محرم صيداً
النص وصححه في شرح الدرر . أن وفي الهداية قالوا والواحد يكفي والمثنى أولى لأنه أحوط وأبعد من الغلط كما في حقوق العباد، وقيل يعتبر المثنى ههنا بالنص اهـ. وفي فتح القدير والذين لم يوجبوه حملوا العدد في الآية على الأولوية لأن المقصود زيادة الإحكام والإتقان والظاهر الوجوب وقصد الإحكام والإتقان لا ينافيه بل قد يكون داعيته ا هـ . وينبغي أن يكتفى بالقاتل إذا كان له معرفة بالقيمة وأن يحمل ذكر الحكمين على الأولوية على قول من يكتفي بالواحد لكنه يتوقف على نقل ولم أره. وكلمه «أو» في قوله أو أقرب المواضع للتوزيع لا للتخيير يعني الحكمين يقومانه في مكان قتله إن كان يباع فيه وفي أقرب المواضع إلى مكان قتله كالبرية. ولا بد من اعتبار المكان ومن اعتبار زمان قتله لاختلاف القيم باختلاف الأمكنة والأزمنة. والضمير في قوله «فيشتري» راجع إلى القاتل فأفاد أنه بعد تقويم الحكمين الخيار للقاتل بين الأشياء الثلاثة ولا خيار للحكمين لأن التخيير شرع رفقاً بمن عليه فيكون الخيار إليه كما في كفارة اليمين وليس في الآية دلالة على اختيارهما لأن قوله أو كفارة أو عدل» بالرفع عطفاً على «جزاء» وليس منصوباً عطفاً على هدياً فاقتضى أن لا خيار لهما في الإطعام والصيام فلزم أن لا خيار لهما في الهدي لعدم القائل بالفصل كما في العناية، أو لأن «هدياً» وقد يقال : جعله إياه متناً واقتصاره عليه يفيد تصحيحه إذ لو اعتقد ضعفه لذكر مقابله تأمل قوله : (وينبغي أن يكتفي الخ) قال أقول في اللباب ويشترط للتقويم عدلان غير الجاني. قال شارحه : على ما نسبه ابن جماعة إلى الحنيفة ولعله لعلة التهمة ا هـ . قوله : (وإن يحمل ذكر الحكمين على الأولوية) الأولى حذفه كما لا يخفى. وقوله على قول من يكتفى متعلقاً بقوله يكتفى» والضمير في قوله «ولم أره للاكتفاء بالقاتل إما حمل ذكر الحكمين على الأولوية فهو منقول ذكره قريباً قوله : (ولا خيار للحكمين نفي لقول محمد الشافعي أن الخيار إلى الحكمين في ذلك فإن حكما بالهدي يجب النظير وإن حكما بالطعام أو بالصيام فعلى ما قال أبو حنيفة وأبو يوسف رحمهما الله من اعتبار القيمة من حيث المعنى. كذا في العناية قوله: (أو) لأن هديا حال الخ) اقتصر من إعراب الآية على موضع الاستدلال وأعربها في الفتح بتمامها فنذكر حاصله أيضاً حالما هنا، وذلك أنه قرئ بتنوين «جزاء» ورفع «مثل» وبدونه على الإضافة البيانية والمعنى واحد أي فجزاء هو مثل ما قتل. ومضمون الآية شرط وجزاء حذف منه المبتدأ بعد فاء الجزاء أو الخبر أي فالواجب جزاء، أو فعليه جزاء، «ومن النعم بيان لـ«ما» أو للعائد إليها أي ما قتله من النعم وهو في موضع الحال، وجملة، «يحكم به صفة فجزاء الذي هو القيمة أو صفة مثل الذي لأن مثلاً لا تتعرف بالإضافة فجاز وصفها ووصف ما أضيف إليها بالجملة . وهدياً حال مقدرة من ضمير (به ) الراجع إلى موصوف الجملة وبالغ الكعبة صفة هدياً» النكرة لأن الإضافة لفظية أو كفارة أو عدل معطوفان على «جزاء» والمعنى على هذا فالواجب عليه جزاء هو قيمة ما قتله من النعم الوحشي يحكم بذلك الجزاء الذي هو القيمة
هو هي
حال كتاب الحج/ فصل إن قتل محرم صيداً من ضمير «به وهي حال مقدرة أي صائراً هديا به وذلك في نفس الأمر بواسطة الشراء بها أو بغير ذلك، وكون الحال مقدرة كثير . وهو وإن لم يلزم على تقدير المخالف فيها يلزم على تقديره في وصفها وهو بالغ الكعبة فإنه لا يصح حكمهما بالهدي موصوفاً ببلوغه إلى الكعبة حال حكمهما به على التحقيق، بل المراد يحكمان به مقدراً بلوغه، فلزوم التقدير ثابت غير أنه يختلف محله على الوجهين. ثم على كل تقدير لا دلالة للآية على أن الاختيار للحكمين بل الظاهر منها أنه إلى من عليه فإن مرجع ضمير المحذوف من الخبر أو متعلق المبتدأ إليه أعني ما قررناه من قولنا فالواجب عليه أو فعليه كذا في فتح القدير. وأشار بقوله «هدياً» إلى أنه لو اختار الهدي لا يذبحه إلا بالحرم الصريح قوله بالغ الكعبة» مع أن الهدي ما يهدى من النعم إلى الحرم، وقول الفقهاء لو قال إن فعلت كذا فثوبي هذا هدي أو إن لبست من غزلك فهو هدي مجاز عن الصدقة بقرينة التقييد بالثوب والغزل والكلام في مطلق الهدي، فلو ذبحه في الحل لا يجزئه عن الهدي بل عن الإطعام فيشترط أن يعطي لك فقير قدر قيمة نصف صاع حنطة أو صاع. من غيرها إن كانت قيمة اللحم مثل قيمة المقتول وإلا فيكمل. وأشار بقوله إن بلغت هدياً إلى أنه إذا وقع الاختيار على الهدي يهدي ما يجزىء في الأضحية حتى لو لم تبلغ قيمة المقتول إلا عناقاً أو حملاً يقوم بالإطعام أو الصوم لا بالهدي ولا يتصور التكفير بالهدي إلا أن تبلغ قيمته جذعاً عظيماً من الضأن أو ثنياً من غيره لأن مطلق الهدي في الشرع ينصرف إلى ما يبلغ ذلك السن لأنه المعهود في إطلاق هدي
الصائرة عدلان حال كونه صائراً هدياً بواسطة القمية أو كفارة الخ. أي الواجب أحد الأمرين من القيمة هدياً ومن الإطعام والصيام المبنيين على تعرف القيمة ا هـ . ملخصاً. ولا يخفى أن مقتضى كلامه أخيراً أن يكون أو عدل معطوفاً على طعام» الذي هو بدل من كفارة أو عطف بيان أو خبر لمحذوف لا على جزاء قوله : (أي صائراً هدياً به الظاهر أن ضمير (به) يعود على الحكم المفهوم من يحكم في الآية وأن ضمير بها) يعود على القيمة المفسر بها الجزاء أو المثل وأن المناسب إسقاط الباء الجارة من قوله «أو بغير ذلك كما في الفتح ليكون عطفاً على الشراء لا على «بواسطة» والمراد بغير الشراء ما يحصل به ملك الهدي من هبة وإرث ونحوهما قوله : (وهو وإن لم يلزم) كأنه جواب سؤال مقدر تقديره سلمنا أن كونها مقدرة كثير لكنه خلاف الأكثر فالأولى كونها مقارنة فيثبت أنه يصير هدياً باختيارهما كما هو قول محمد والشافعي. فأجاب بأن كونها مقدرة في الآية وإن لم يلزمهما على ما قرراه فيها لكنه لازم في وصفها وهو بالغ الكعبة لظهور أن بلوغه الكعبة متراخ عن الحكم بكونه هدياً قوله : (يقوم بالإطعام الخ) قال في اللباب : ولا يجوز الصغار كالجفرة والعناق والحمل إلا على وجه الإطعام بأن يعطي كل فقير ما يساوي قيمة نصف صاع من بر قوله : (كما قدمناه) أي قريباً من مسألة الثوب والغزل قوله : (وأشار بقوله كالفطرة الخ) قال في شرح اللباب: وهل يشترط عدد
The chapter of Hajj / Section: If a muhrim kills game. The text: And it was corrected in Sharh al-Durar. In al-Hidayah they said: one suffices and two is better because it is more cautious and further from error as in the rights of servants. It was said that two are considered here by text. In Fath al-Qadir: those who did not oblige it carried the number in the verse on preference because the aim is increased precision and accuracy, and apparent is obligation, and the intent of precision does not negate it but may be its motive. And it is preferable that the killer suffice if he has knowledge of value, and that mentioning the two arbiters be carried on preference according to the one who suffices with one, but it depends on transmission and I have not seen it. His word 'or' in 'or the nearest place' is for distribution not choice, meaning the two arbiters evaluate it in the place of killing if it can be sold there, and in the nearest place to the place of killing like the desert. It is necessary to consider the place and time of killing due to differing values by different places and times. The pronoun in 'he buys' refers to the killer, so it indicates that after the evaluation of the two arbiters, the choice is for the killer among the three things, and there is no choice for the two arbiters because the choice was legislated as a leniency for the one obligated, so the choice belongs to him as in the expiation of an oath. And there is no indication in the verse for their choice because His saying 'or expiation or justice' is in the nominative as an adjunct to 'penalty' and not accusative as an adjunct to 'a sacrificial animal', so it necessitates that they have no choice in feeding and fasting, so it follows they have no choice in the sacrificial animal because no one distinguishes between them as in al-Inayah, or because...
Source pages p. 53

Commentary
This passage is an expansion of the ruling on a muhrim who kills game. The author discusses two main issues: (1) the number and qualification of the arbiters who evaluate the value of the killed game, and (2) who has the choice among the three expiation options (sacrificial animal, feeding the poor, or fasting). The Hanafi position is that two just witnesses (عدلان) are required for valuation, though one is sufficient by some transmissions. The valuation must be done at the place and time of killing because market values differ. After valuation, the choice of which expiation to perform lies entirely with the killer, not with the two arbiters. This is supported by analogy with the expiation of an oath and by the grammatical analysis of the Quranic verse (5:95). The passage refutes the view of Muhammad ibn al-Hasan al-Shaybani and al-Shafi'i that the arbiters have the choice. It also clarifies that if the killer chooses a sacrificial animal, it must be slaughtered in the sacred precinct (al-Haram) and must meet the age requirements for an udhiyah (sacrificial animal). Young animals like a kid or lamb do not qualify as هدي but contribute to the feeding option instead.

Key Terms
جزاء (jazā’): The penalty or compensation for killing game while in ihram, which is a value equivalent to the animal killed.
مثل (mithl): An equivalent animal from livestock that resembles the killed game in value or characteristics.
هدي (hady): A sacrificial animal that is offered in the Sacred Precinct (al-Haram) as expiation.
عدلان (ʿadlān): Two just witnesses or arbiters who evaluate the value of the killed game.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, after the two just arbiters evaluate the value of game killed by a muhrim, who has the choice among the three expiation options (sacrificial animal, feeding the poor, or fasting)?
A) The two arbiters (الحكمان) make the choice.
B) The killer (القاتل) makes the choice.
C) The choice is determined by the closest market.
D) The poor recipients of the expiation make the choice.

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, the killer of game while in ihram has the choice among three expiations after two just witnesses evaluate the value; the arbiters only determine the value, not the type of expiation.

Feeding in Jaza' al-Sayd: Amount and Conditions Analogized to Fitrah
Explaining the analogy between jaza' al-sayd feeding and fitrah.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the amount of food required per poor person in jaza' al-sayd feeding and explain which conditions are analogized from Zakat al-Fitr and which are not, including the disputed issue of tamlik vs. ibahah.

Core Idea
The feeding penalty for hunting is like Fitrah in amount, but permissive use (ibahah) suffices, unlike Fitrah.

The author of Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq unpacks the statement of Kanz al-Daqa'iq that the feeding option in jaza' al-sayd is 'like the Fitrah'. This lesson navigates the precise scope of that analogy: the quantity per poor, the number of recipients, the permissibility of giving value, and the critical distinction that while Fitrah requires ownership transfer (tamlik), jaza' al-sayd feeding is valid with mere permissive use (ibahah). By understanding this qiyas jaliy, you learn how Hanafi scholars delimit analogical reasoning to only those aspects that share a common effective cause.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Ruling on Amount
The passage states that each poor receives half a sa' of wheat or one sa' of dates/barley. Confirm this as the minimum and understand that excess is voluntary.
This is directly analogized from Fitrah.
2
Note the Conditions on Number of Recipients
Unlike Fitrah, the feeding in jaza' al-sayd must be distributed to a number of poor (at least six if three sa' are given). Giving all to one poor in one day is invalid, but spreading over days is valid.
This is deduced from the text's 'each poor' and the minimum number of poor in the verse.
3
Appreciate the Dispute on Ibahah vs Tamlik
Imam al-Aspijiabi holds that ibahah (inviting to eat without ownership) suffices, while al-Karkhi and others argue tamlik is required. The author sides with al-Aspijiabi, limiting the analogy to amount only.
The qiyas is not comprehensive; similarity in illa (obligatory expiation) does not extend to all sub-rulings.
4
Apply the Permissibility of Giving Value
Paying the cash equivalent of half a sa' per poor is allowed, following the same analogy to Fitrah.
Value may be given in place of grain, but the distribution rules remain.
5
Recognize the Excluded Recipients
Just like Fitrah, one cannot give jaza' al-sayd feeding to one's own ascendants, descendants, or spouse, nor to those whose testimony is not accepted.
These rules are taken from the general principles of obligatory charity.

Source Text

وأشار بقوله ((كالفطرة إلى أنه يطعم كل مسكين نصف صاع من بر أو صاعاً من تمر أو شعير، وليس له أن يطعم واحداً أقل منه ، وله أن يطعم أكثر تبرعاً حتى لا يحتسب الزيادة من القيمة كيلا ينتقص عدد المساكين هكذا ذكره ههنا وقد حققنا في باب صدقة الفطر أنه يجوز أن يفرق نصف الصاع على مساكين على المذهب وأن القائل بالمنع الكرخي فينبغي أن يكون كذلك هنا ،خصوصاً، والنص هنا مطلق فيجري على إطلاقه لكن لا يجوز أن يعطي لمسكين واحد كالفطرة لأن العدد منصوص عليه وإلى أنه يجوز التصدق على الذمي كالمسلم الحكم في المشبه به والمسلم أحب، وإلى أنه لا يجوز أن يتصدق بجزاء الصيد على أصله وإن علا، وفرعه وإن سفل وزوجته وزوجها كما هو الحكم في كل صدقة واجبة كما أسلفناه في باب المصرف. وصرحوا هنا بأنه لا يجوز التصدق بشيء من جزاء الصيد على من لا تقبل شهادته له وما ذكرناه أولى لكن يرد على المصنف أن الإباحة تكفي في جزاء الصيد في الإطعام كالتمليك كما صرح به الإمام الأسبيجابي، ولا يكفي في الفطرة. وأشار أيضاً بقوله «كالفطرة إلى أن دفع القيمة جائز فيدفع لكل مسكين قيمة نصف صاع من بر، ولا كما هو المساكين صورة في الإطعام تمليكاً وإباحة؟ قال أصحابنا : ليس بشرط حتى لو دفع طعام ستة مساكين وهو ثلاثة أصع إلى مسكين واحد في ستة أيام كل يوم نصف صاع أو غدى مسكيناً واحداً أو عشاه ستة أيام أجزأه عندنا ، أما لو دفع طعام ستة مساكين إلى مسكين واحد في يوم دفعة واحدة أو دفعات فلا رواية فيه، واختلف مشايخنا فقال بعضهم يجوز ، وقال عامتهم لا يجوز إلا عن واحد وعليه الفتوى ا هـ . وبه قوله : (فينبغي أن يكون كذلك هنا تابعه عليه في النهر ولا يخفى أنه بحث مع المنقول قوله : (كما هو الحكم في المشبه به تقدم في المصرف أن فيه خلاف أبي يوسف وذكرنا عن الحاوي أنه قال : نأخذ قوله : (وما ذكرناه (أولى كان وجه الأولوية أنه يلزم على ما قالوه أن لا يجوز التصدق به على شريكه لأنه لا تقبل شهادته له فيما هو من شركتهما لكن نفي القبول ينصرف إلى الكامل وهو عدم القبول مطلقاً والشريك ليس كذلك بل تقبل في الجملة قوله : لكن يرد على المصنف الخ) قال في النهر : قد عرف أن المشبه لا يلزم أن يعطى حكم المشبه به من كل وجه على أن الظاهر أن التشبيه إنما هو في المقدار كما جرى عليه الشارح وغيره ا هـ . ثم الإباحة بالوضع والعرض للفقير وهذا عند
And he indicated by his saying 'like the Fitrah' that he feeds each poor person half a sa' of wheat or one sa' of dates or barley, and he may not feed anyone less than that, but he may feed more voluntarily. He may not count the excess from the value so that the number of poor is not reduced. This is mentioned here, and we have verified in the chapter on Zakat al-Fitr that it is permissible to distribute half a sa' among the poor according to the madhhab, and that the one who prohibits it is al-Karkhi. So it should be the same here, especially since the text here is absolute and should be applied absolutely, but it is not permissible to give to one poor person like Fitrah because the number is specified. And [he indicated] that it is permissible to give charity to a Dhimmi like a Muslim according to the ruling of the analogized-to, but a Muslim is more beloved. And that it is not permissible to give charity from the penalty of game to his ascendant even if high, nor his descendant even if low, nor his wife nor her husband, just as in every obligatory charity as we have mentioned in the chapter on expenditure. And they stated here that it is not permissible to give anything from the jaza' al-sayd to one whose testimony is not accepted for him, and what we mentioned is better. But an objection to the author is that permissibility (ibahah) is sufficient in jaza' al-sayd feeding like ownership (tamlik) as stated by Imam al-Aspijiabi, and it is not sufficient in Fitrah. And he also indicated by his saying 'like the Fitrah' that giving the value is permissible, so he gives to each poor the value of half a sa' of wheat, but not like the picture of the poor in feeding as ownership or permissibility? Our companions said: it is not a condition, such that if he gave the food of six poor, being three sa', to one poor in six days, each day half a sa', or if he gave lunch or dinner to one poor for six days, it suffices according to us. But if he gave the food of six poor to one poor in one day, either at once or in installments, there is no narration on it, and our shuyukh differed: some said it is permissible, and the majority said it is not permissible except for one, and the fatwa is on that. And with that, his saying: 'So it should be the same here' – he followed him in al-Nahr, and it is not hidden that it is a discussion with the transmitted. His saying: 'As is the ruling in the analogized-to' – it was mentioned in the expenditure chapter that there is a difference from Abu Yusuf, and we mentioned from al-Hawi that he said: we adopt. His saying: 'And what we mentioned is better' – the aspect of being better is that on what they said, it would not be permissible to give charity to his partner because his testimony for him is not accepted in what pertains to their partnership, but the negation of acceptance refers to complete acceptance, which is absolute non-acceptance, and the partner is not like that; rather it is accepted in some cases. His saying: 'But there is an objection to the author' – he said in al-Nahr: it is known that the analogized element does not necessarily have to take the same ruling as the analogized-to in every respect, rather the apparent is that the analogy is only in the amount as the sharh and others have proceeded. Then permissibility (ibahah) is by placing and presenting to the poor, and this is when...
Source pages p. 55

Commentary
This passage is an expansion probe from Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq commenting on the statement of Kanz al-Daqa'iq that the feeding penalty for a muhrim who kills game is like Zakat al-Fitr. The author, Imam Ibn Nujaym, explains what this analogy means. First, the amount: each poor person receives half a sa' of wheat (the best quality grain) or one sa' of inferior grains like dates or barley. This is the same as Fitrah. Second, the number of poor: unlike Fitrah, the text says 'each poor' implying a condition of number, so one cannot give all the food to a single poor person at once; the minimum number is six poor persons for three sa' (as will be clarified). However, the author notes that if one spreads the food over six days, giving half a sa' each day to the same poor person, it is valid. Third, giving value: it is permissible to give the cash value of half a sa' per poor, based on the same analogy. Fourth, the recipient: a Dhimmi may receive, though a Muslim is preferred. Fifth, relatives: just as in other obligatory charity, one cannot give to one's own ascendants, descendants, or spouse. Sixth, the condition of ownership vs. permissibility: a subtle point—in Fitrah, ownership (tamlik) is required, but in jaza' al-sayd, permissibility of use (ibahah) suffices, such as inviting the poor to eat without giving them possession. The author defends his analogy by noting that simile (tashbih) need not be complete; it suffices in the amount. He also discusses a disputed case: if one gives the food of six poor (three sa') to one poor person in one day, the majority of later scholars say it is not allowed except as for one day, but there is a narration allowing it. He concludes with al-Nahr's explanation that analogy is only in quantity, not in all conditions.

Key Terms
جزاء الصيد (jaza' al-sayd): The penalty (kaffarah) required from a muhrim who kills game, which is an option of sacrificing an animal, feeding the poor, or fasting
الفطرة (al-fitrah): Zakat al-Fitr, the obligatory charity at the end of Ramadan
الإباحة (al-ibahah): Permissibility of use without ownership transfer; in feeding the poor, it means allowing them to eat without giving them the food in ownership

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Based on the passage, which of the following is true about giving value (qimah) in jaza' al-sayd feeding?
A) Value cannot be given; only grain is acceptable.
B) Value may be given, but only if no grain is available.
C) Value may be given freely, analogous to Fitrah.
D) Value may be given only for barley, not wheat.

Key Takeaway
The analogy to Fitrah in jaza' al-sayd feeding applies primarily to the quantity (half sa' per poor), not to every condition; ibahah suffices, and giving value is allowed.

Leftover Less Than Half Sa': Choice of Charity or Fasting
Ruling on leftover less than half sa' with talil and distinction from oath expiation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling when less than half a sa' remains from jaza' al-sayd feeding and explain why fasting is an original option that can be combined with feeding.

Core Idea
When the feeding measure falls short, fasting is an equal original option, not a substitute.

This lesson examines a common scenario: after fulfilling the required number of poor for feeding in game compensation, a surplus of less than half a sa' remains. What is the ruling? The Hanafi school provides a clear choice between charity or fasting, and even allows combining both. Understanding this ruling requires distinguishing jaza' al-sayd from oath expiation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario
The muhrim killed game and must feed six poor with half sa' each. After feeding some, less than half a sa' remains (the surplus). Determine what is wajib on him.
The surplus is less than the minimum per poor (half sa').
2
Apply the principle of watr (odd amount)
He must observe both the measure (amount) and the number of poor. Since the amount cannot be fully observed, it drops, but the number can be observed by giving to one poor. Hence he has a choice: give the surplus to one poor as charity, or fast one day.
Fasting less than a day is not valid, so a full day is required.
3
Distinguish from oath expiation
In kaffarat al-yamin, the amount per poor is fixed at half sa' and cannot vary. In jaza' al-sayd, the value varies, so flexibility exists.
4
Analyze the combination of feeding and fasting
The text permits combining both methods (e.g., feed some days and fast others) because fasting is an original option like feeding, not a substitute. Contrast with oath expiation where fasting is a substitute and cannot be combined with the primary option.
This is based on the Quran (5:95) listing three equal alternatives.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولو فضل أقل من نصف صاع تصدق به أو صام يوماً وإن جرحه أو قطع عضوه أو نتف شعره ضمن ما نقص وتجب القيمة بنتف ريشه وقطع قوائمه وحلبه وكسر بيضه يجوز النقص عنها كما في العين كما صرحوا به في مسألة ذبح الهدي في الحل فإنه يجزئه باعتبار القيمة كما قدمناه . قوله : (ولو) فضل أقل من نصف صاع تصدق به أو صام يوماً) لأن الواجب عليه مراعاة المقدار وعدد المساكين وقد عجز عن مراعاة المقدار فسقط وقدر على مراعاة العدد فلزمه ما قدر عليه بخلاف كفارة اليمين لأنها مقدرة بإطعام عشرة مساكين، كل مسكين لا نصف صاع يزيد ولا ينقص. أما القيمة هنا تزيد وتنقص فيخير إن شاء تصدق به على مسكين وإن شاء صام يوماً كاملاً لأن الصوم أقل من يوم غير مشروع. وأشار إلى أن الواجب لو كان دون طعام مسكين بأن قتل يربوعاً أو عصفوراً فهو مخير أيضاً، وإلى أنه يجوز الجمع بين الصوم والإطعام بخلاف كفارة اليمين والفرق أن في كفارة الصيد الصوم أصل كالإطعام حتى يجوز الصوم مع القدرة على الإطعام فجاز الجمع بينهما وإكمال أحدهما بالآخر، وأما في كفارة اليمين فالصوم بدل عن التكفير بالمال حتى لا يجوز المصير إليه مع القدرة على المال فلا يجوز الجمع بين الأصل والبدل للتنافي . وشمل كلامه ما إذا كان هذا الفاضل من جنس ما فعله أولاً حتى لو اختار الهدي وفضل من القيمة ما لا يبلغ هدياً فهو مخير في الفضل أيضاً. وعلى هذا لو بلغت قيمته هديين إن شاء ذبحهما، وإن شاء تصدق بالطعام، وإن شاء صام عن كل نصف صاع يوماً، وإن شاء ذبح أحدهما وأطعم وصام بقي فيجمع بين الأنواع الثلاثة أو يتصدق بالقيمة من الدراهم أو الدنانير. وذكر الولوالجي في فتاواه أن المعتبر في الطعام قيمة الصيد، وفي الصوم قيمة الطعام، وهكذا في البدائع قوله : (وإن جرحه أو قطع عضوه أو نتف شعره ضمن ما نقص اعتباراً للبعض بالكل كما في حقوق العباد أفاد بمقابلة الجرح للقتل المتقدم أنه لم يمت من هذا الجرح لأنه لو مات منه عما أبي يوسف خلافاً لمحمد وعن أبي حنيفة روايتان والأصح أنه مع الأول لكن هذا الخلاف في كفارة الحلق من الأذى، وأما كفارة الصيد فيجوز الإطعام على وجه الإباحة بلا خلاف فيضع لهم طعاماً ويمكنهم منه حتى يستوفوا أكلتين مشبعتين غداء وعشاء، أو سحوراً وعشاء، أو غدائين أو عشاءين، لكن الأول أولى فإن غداهم لا غير أو عشاهم فقط لا يجزئه لكن إن غداهم وأعطاهم قيمة العشاء أو بالعكس جاز، والمستحب أن يكون مأدوماً، وفي الهداية لا بد من الإدام في خبز الشعير. وفي المصفى : غير البر لا يجوز إلا بإدام. وفي البدائع : يستوي كون الطعام مادوماً أو غير مأدوم حتى لو غداهم وعشاهم خبزاً بلا إدام أجزأه وكذا لو أطعم خبز الشعير أو سويقاً أو تمراً لأن ذلك قد يؤكل وحده. ثم المعتبر هو الشبع التام لا مقدار الطعام حتى لو قدم أربعة أرغفة أو ثلاثة بين يدي ستة مساكين وشبعوا أجزأه وإن لم يبلغ ذلك صاعاً أو نصف صاع ولو كان أحدهم شبعان قيل لا
And if less than half a sa' remains, he gives it as charity or fasts one day. And if he wounds it, or cuts its limb, or plucks its feathers, he is liable for the deficiency. And value is due for plucking its feathers, cutting its legs, milking it, and breaking its eggs. It is permissible to decrease from it just as in the case of the commodity ('ayn), as they stated in the issue of slaughtering the hady in the halal, for it suffices by consideration of value as we have presented. His saying (and if less than half a sa' remains, give it as charity or fast one day) because he is obligated to observe the measure and the number of poor, and he is incapable of observing the measure, so it drops, but he is able to observe the number, so what he is able to do becomes incumbent. This is unlike kaffarat al-yamin (oath expiation) because it is specified by feeding ten poor, each poor not less nor more than half a sa'. As for the value here, it increases and decreases, so he has a choice: if he wishes, he gives it as charity to one poor, or if he wishes, he fasts a complete day, because fasting less than a day is not legislated. And he indicated that if the wajib is less than the food of one poor, such as killing a jerboa or a sparrow, he also has a choice, and that it is permissible to combine fasting and feeding, unlike kaffarat al-yamin. The difference is that in the kaffarah of game, fasting is an original option like feeding, such that fasting is permissible even while able to feed, so combining both is permitted and completing one with the other. But in kaffarat al-yamin, fasting is an alternative to expiation with wealth, so it is not permissible to resort to it while able to give wealth, so combining the original and the alternative is not permitted due to conflict. And his statement includes the case where this surplus is of the same type as what he did initially, such that if he chose the hady and a surplus of value that does not constitute a hady remains, he is also given a choice in the surplus. Similarly, if its value amounts to two hadys, he may slaughter both if he wishes, or give food if he wishes, or fast for each half sa' a day if he wishes, or slaughter one and feed and fast the remainder, thus combining the three types, or he may give the value in dirhams or dinars. And al-Walwaliji mentioned in his Fatawa that the consideration in food is the value of the game, and in fasting the value of the food. And likewise in al-Bada'i. His saying (and if he wounds it, or cuts its limb, or plucks its feathers, he is liable for the deficiency, considering the part as the whole just as in the rights of humans. He indicated by contrasting wounding with the preceding killing that he did not die from this wound, because if he died from it, then... Abu Yusuf opposed Muhammad, and from Abu Hanifa there are two narrations, but the sounder is with the first. But this difference is in the kaffarah of shaving from harm (hajj). As for the kaffarah of game, it is permissible to feed on the basis of ibahah without disagreement. He places food for them and enables them so that they eat two satisfying meals: lunch and dinner, or suhur and dinner, or two lunches or two dinners, but the first is better. If he gives only lunch or only dinner, it does not suffice. However, if he gives them lunch and gives them the value of dinner, or vice versa, it is permissible. It is recommended that the food be seasoned. In al-Hidayah, seasoning is necessary for barley bread. In al-Musaffa: other than wheat is not permissible except with seasoning. In al-Bada'i: the same whether the food is seasoned or not, even if he gives them lunch and dinner with bread without seasoning, it suffices. Similarly, if he feeds barley bread or sawiq or dates, because these may be eaten alone. Then the consideration is complete satiation, not the quantity of food, such that if he presents four or three loaves to six poor and they become full, it suffices, even if that does not amount to a sa' or half a sa'. And if one of them was already full, it is said no.
Source pages p. 56

Commentary
This expansion probe contains two distinct rulings within the chapter on a muhrim killing game. First ruling: if after fulfilling the required feeding there is leftover less than half a sa' (the minimum per poor), the person has a choice: either give that leftover as charity to a poor person, or fast one day. This is because the original obligation considered two factors: the amount (half sa') and the number of poor (six). Since the amount cannot be fully observed, it drops, but the number can be observed by giving to one poor, and the leftover is less than the minimum, so the choice is given. This differs from oath expiation (kaffarat al-yamin) where the amount per poor is fixed and not elastic. The author notes that if the entire wajib is less than one poor's share (e.g., killing a small bird), the person is also free to choose feeding or fasting, and may even combine them, unlike oath expiation where fasting is a mere substitute and cannot be combined with the primary option. Second ruling: compensation for injuring game (wounding, cutting limb, plucking feathers, etc.) is assessed by the reduction in market value (damage). This is analogous to liability for property damage among humans. The value of the game before injury is compared to after, and the difference is owed. This can be in cash or kind. The author then embarks on a lengthy side-discussion about the method of feeding when using ibahah (invitation to eat). He reviews different opinions on the requirement of seasoning, satiation, and the number of meals. The reliable position is that complete satisfaction (shab') is the criterion, not a fixed amount; if the poor are full, it suffices even if the quantity is less than half sa'. The issue of feeding a person who is already full is left unresolved (قيل لا).

Key Terms
كفارة اليمين (kaffarat al-yamin): Expiation for breaking a valid oath, consisting of feeding ten poor or clothing them or freeing a slave
اليربوع (al-yarbu'): A type of small rodent (jerboa), used as an example of small game

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In jaza' al-sayd, when less than half sa' remains, what is the ruling?
A) Nothing is required; the surplus is void.
B) He must complete it to half sa' by adding from his own food.
C) He may give it to one poor or fast one day.
D) He must feed all six poor equally.

Key Takeaway
When the feeding measure is short, the obligation shifts to number, giving the pilgrim a choice between charity or fasting, and both may be combined.

Injury to Game: Compensation Based on Reduction in Value
Ruling on injury to game: liability for reduction in value, with intra-Hanafi differences.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state that injury to game while in ihram incurs liability for the reduction in market value, and distinguish it from killing.

Core Idea
Partial injury to game is compensated by the decrease in value, not a fixed penalty.

This lesson covers a common scenario: a muhrim wounds or harms game without killing it. The ruling is that he must pay compensation equal to the reduction in the animal's market value. This principle is analogous to property damage among humans. The passage also explains how to assess this value and nuances of the feeding method when compensation takes the form of food.

Guided Path
1
Identify the harmful act
Wounding, cutting a limb, plucking feathers, milking, or breaking eggs all cause a loss in the game's value.
The act does not include killing, which has a separate ruling (full penalty).
2
Apply the rule of compensation for partial damage
The muhrim is liable for the amount by which the game's value decreases due to his action. This is measured by comparing market value before and after the injury.
This is analogous to damages in civil liability (huquq al-ibad).
3
Note the intra-madhhab difference
If the injury leads to death, there is a difference: Abu Yusuf holds the muhrim liable for the full game penalty if the wound was fatal, while Muhammad says he is only liable for the injury reduction. The sounder view follows Abu Yusuf.
This difference, however, pertains to kaffarah of shaving from harm, not directly game penalty according to some.
4
Consider the feeding method if payment is food
When compensation is paid by feeding, the method is ibahah (inviting to eat). The poor must be satiated. The passage discusses nuances like seasoning and number of meals.
Complete satisfaction (shab') is the criterion, not fixed quantity.

Feeding Method in Jaza' al-Sayd: Ibahah, Satiation, and Seasoning
Dispute on feeding method: ibahah, meals, seasoning, and satiation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to describe the Hanafi method of feeding the poor in jaza' al-sayd using ibahah, identify the criterion of satiation, and evaluate the dispute on seasoning.

Core Idea
Feeding the poor in game penalty is by invitation (ibahah), and complete satiation, not quantity, is the measure.

When compensation for killing or injuring game is paid by feeding, the Hanafi school specifies a particular method: ibahah (invitation to eat). This lesson explores the details: how many meals, requirement of seasoning, and the crucial principle that satiation (shab') is the standard, not a fixed amount of food. The passage reviews internal differences on seasoning, settling on the view that satiation alone suffices.

Guided Path
1
Understand the method of feeding
The feeder must invite the poor (ibahah) and enable them to eat until they are full. This differs from transferring ownership (tamlik).
Ibahah is sufficient; the poor do not need to own the food.
2
Determine the number and timing of meals
Two satisfying meals are required: e.g., lunch and dinner. Alternatives like suhur and dinner, or two lunches, are allowed but the first is preferred.
A single meal does not suffice unless the poor are given the value of the missing meal.
3
Address the seasoning requirement
There is disagreement: some Hanafi authorities (al-Hidayah, al-Musaffa) require seasoning (idam) for certain grains like barley. Others (al-Bada'i) deem it unnecessary as long as the food can be eaten alone.
The author follows al-Bada'i, allowing food without seasoning if it is normally eaten alone.
4
Apply the satiation criterion
Complete satiation is the measure, not a fixed quantity. Even a small amount of food that fills the poor suffices, even if less than half sa'.
This is a key Hanafi position distinguishing jaza' from zakat al-fitr.

Source Text

كالإطعام حتى يجوز الصوم مع القدرة على الإطعام فجاز الجمع بينهما وإكمال أحدهما بالآخر، وأما في كفارة اليمين فالصوم بدل عن التكفير بالمال حتى لا يجوز المصير إليه مع القدرة على المال فلا يجوز الجمع بين الأصل والبدل للتنافي . وشمل كلامه ما إذا كان هذا الفاضل من جنس ما فعله أولاً حتى لو اختار الهدي وفضل من القيمة ما لا يبلغ هدياً فهو مخير في الفضل أيضاً. وعلى هذا لو بلغت قيمته هديين إن شاء ذبحهما، وإن شاء تصدق بالطعام، وإن شاء صام عن كل نصف صاع يوماً، وإن شاء ذبح أحدهما وأطعم وصام بقي فيجمع بين الأنواع الثلاثة أو يتصدق بالقيمة من الدراهم أو الدنانير. وذكر الولوالجي في فتاواه أن المعتبر في الطعام قيمة الصيد، وفي الصوم قيمة الطعام، وهكذا في البدائع قوله : (وإن جرحه أو قطع عضوه أو نتف شعره ضمن ما نقص اعتباراً للبعض بالكل كما في حقوق العباد أفاد بمقابلة الجرح للقتل المتقدم أنه لم يمت من هذا الجرح لأنه لو مات منه عما أبي يوسف خلافاً لمحمد وعن أبي حنيفة روايتان والأصح أنه مع الأول لكن هذا الخلاف في كفارة الحلق من الأذى، وأما كفارة الصيد فيجوز الإطعام على وجه الإباحة بلا خلاف فيضع لهم طعاماً ويمكنهم منه حتى يستوفوا أكلتين مشبعتين غداء وعشاء، أو سحوراً وعشاء، أو غدائين أو عشاءين، لكن الأول أولى فإن غداهم لا غير أو عشاهم فقط لا يجزئه لكن إن غداهم وأعطاهم قيمة العشاء أو بالعكس جاز، والمستحب أن يكون مأدوماً، وفي الهداية لا بد من الإدام في خبز الشعير. وفي المصفى : غير البر لا يجوز إلا بإدام. وفي البدائع : يستوي كون الطعام مادوماً أو غير مأدوم حتى لو غداهم وعشاهم خبزاً بلا إدام أجزأه وكذا لو أطعم خبز الشعير أو سويقاً أو تمراً لأن ذلك قد يؤكل وحده. ثم المعتبر هو الشبع التام لا مقدار الطعام حتى لو قدم أربعة أرغفة أو ثلاثة بين يدي ستة مساكين وشبعوا أجزأه وإن لم يبلغ ذلك صاعاً أو نصف صاع ولو كان أحدهم شبعان قيل لا
And if less than half a sa' remains, he gives it as charity or fasts one day. And if he wounds it, or cuts its limb, or plucks its feathers, he is liable for the deficiency. And value is due for plucking its feathers, cutting its legs, milking it, and breaking its eggs. It is permissible to decrease from it just as in the case of the commodity ('ayn), as they stated in the issue of slaughtering the hady in the halal, for it suffices by consideration of value as we have presented. His saying (and if less than half a sa' remains, give it as charity or fast one day) because he is obligated to observe the measure and the number of poor, and he is incapable of observing the measure, so it drops, but he is able to observe the number, so what he is able to do becomes incumbent. This is unlike kaffarat al-yamin (oath expiation) because it is specified by feeding ten poor, each poor not less nor more than half a sa'. As for the value here, it increases and decreases, so he has a choice: if he wishes, he gives it as charity to one poor, or if he wishes, he fasts a complete day, because fasting less than a day is not legislated. And he indicated that if the wajib is less than the food of one poor, such as killing a jerboa or a sparrow, he also has a choice, and that it is permissible to combine fasting and feeding, unlike kaffarat al-yamin. The difference is that in the kaffarah of game, fasting is an original option like feeding, such that fasting is permissible even while able to feed, so combining both is permitted and completing one with the other. But in kaffarat al-yamin, fasting is an alternative to expiation with wealth, so it is not permissible to resort to it while able to give wealth, so combining the original and the alternative is not permitted due to conflict. And his statement includes the case where this surplus is of the same type as what he did initially, such that if he chose the hady and a surplus of value that does not constitute a hady remains, he is also given a choice in the surplus. Similarly, if its value amounts to two hadys, he may slaughter both if he wishes, or give food if he wishes, or fast for each half sa' a day if he wishes, or slaughter one and feed and fast the remainder, thus combining the three types, or he may give the value in dirhams or dinars. And al-Walwaliji mentioned in his Fatawa that the consideration in food is the value of the game, and in fasting the value of the food. And likewise in al-Bada'i. His saying (and if he wounds it, or cuts its limb, or plucks its feathers, he is liable for the deficiency, considering the part as the whole just as in the rights of humans. He indicated by contrasting wounding with the preceding killing that he did not die from this wound, because if he died from it, then... Abu Yusuf opposed Muhammad, and from Abu Hanifa there are two narrations, but the sounder is with the first. But this difference is in the kaffarah of shaving from harm (hajj). As for the kaffarah of game, it is permissible to feed on the basis of ibahah without disagreement. He places food for them and enables them so that they eat two satisfying meals: lunch and dinner, or suhur and dinner, or two lunches or two dinners, but the first is better. If he gives only lunch or only dinner, it does not suffice. However, if he gives them lunch and gives them the value of dinner, or vice versa, it is permissible. It is recommended that the food be seasoned. In al-Hidayah, seasoning is necessary for barley bread. In al-Musaffa: other than wheat is not permissible except with seasoning. In al-Bada'i: the same whether the food is seasoned or not, even if he gives them lunch and dinner with bread without seasoning, it suffices. Similarly, if he feeds barley bread or sawiq or dates, because these may be eaten alone. Then the consideration is complete satiation, not the quantity of food, such that if he presents four or three loaves to six poor and they become full, it suffices, even if that does not amount to a sa' or half a sa'. And if one of them was already full, it is said no.
Source pages p. 56

Commentary
This expansion probe contains two distinct rulings within the chapter on a muhrim killing game. First ruling: if after fulfilling the required feeding there is leftover less than half a sa' (the minimum per poor), the person has a choice: either give that leftover as charity to a poor person, or fast one day. This is because the original obligation considered two factors: the amount (half sa') and the number of poor (six). Since the amount cannot be fully observed, it drops, but the number can be observed by giving to one poor, and the leftover is less than the minimum, so the choice is given. This differs from oath expiation (kaffarat al-yamin) where the amount per poor is fixed and not elastic. The author notes that if the entire wajib is less than one poor's share (e.g., killing a small bird), the person is also free to choose feeding or fasting, and may even combine them, unlike oath expiation where fasting is a mere substitute and cannot be combined with the primary option. Second ruling: compensation for injuring game (wounding, cutting limb, plucking feathers, etc.) is assessed by the reduction in market value (damage). This is analogous to liability for property damage among humans. The value of the game before injury is compared to after, and the difference is owed. This can be in cash or kind. The author then embarks on a lengthy side-discussion about the method of feeding when using ibahah (invitation to eat). He reviews different opinions on the requirement of seasoning, satiation, and the number of meals. The reliable position is that complete satisfaction (shab') is the criterion, not a fixed amount; if the poor are full, it suffices even if the quantity is less than half sa'. The issue of feeding a person who is already full is left unresolved (قيل لا).

Key Terms
الإباحة (al-ibahah): In feeding the poor, it refers to inviting them to eat without transferring ownership

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the criterion for feeding in jaza' al-sayd according to the Hanafi school?
A) Each poor must receive exactly half a sa' of grain.
B) The poor must be completely full (shab' tamm).
C) The food must be seasoned.
D) The food must be given as a gift (tamlik).

Key Takeaway
Feeding in jaza' al-sayd is by invitation (ibahah) and the goal is satiation, not a fixed quantity, with seasoning recommended but not required.
