Ruling on Excess Less Than Half a Sa' in Hunting Kaffarah
Explanation of the ruling when excess compensation is less than half a sa', with options to give charity or fast.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the options for the excess compensation in hunting kaffarah when it is less than half a sa', and explain why the ruling differs from oath kaffarah.

Core Idea
In hunting kaffarah, excess less than half a sa' can be given as charity to one poor or fast one day, because the obligation considers both quantity and number.

This lesson unpacks a nuanced ruling from Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq regarding the compensation (kaffarah) for a muhrim who kills game during ihram. When the obligation involves feeding the poor and an excess amount remains that is less than half a sa' (the minimum per poor person), the Hanafi school provides clear options. This passage also highlights the key distinction between hunting kaffarah and oath kaffarah, demonstrating the school's method of legal reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario and the obligation
Understand that the muhrim must compensate for killing game. The compensation can be by sacrificing an equivalent animal, feeding the poor, or fasting. The obligation involves both a quantity (food) and a number of poor people.
The base ruling is from Quran 5:95.
2
Understand the excess less than half a sa'
If after fulfilling part of the feeding obligation, an excess remains that is less than half a sa', the muhrim cannot complete a full feeding unit for another poor person. The text rules that he may either give that excess as charity to one poor or fast one day.
Half a sa' is the minimum per poor person in such compensations.
3
Grasp the underlying rationale
The obligation is to consider both the quantity and the number of poor. If the muhrim is unable to complete the quantity (due to the small excess), he can still satisfy the number by giving to one poor or fasting.
This differs from oath kaffarah where the quantity is fixed and cannot be split.
4
Contrast with oath kaffarah
In oath kaffarah, the feeding amount is fixed at half a sa' per poor, and fasting is a substitute only when unable to feed. Hence, no such flexibility exists.
The comparison helps to understand the specificity of hunting kaffarah.
5
Apply to extended scenarios
If the whole obligation is less than the food of one poor (e.g., killing a small animal), the muhrim is also given the choice between feeding that amount or fasting. If the value allows for multiple sacrifices, he may slaughter multiple, feed, fast, or combine.
The principle of takhayyur (choice) applies broadly.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (ولو) فضل أقل من نصف صاع تصدق به أو صام يوماً) لأن الواجب عليه مراعاة المقدار وعدد المساكين وقد عجز عن مراعاة المقدار فسقط وقدر على مراعاة العدد فلزمه ما قدر عليه بخلاف كفارة اليمين لأنها مقدرة بإطعام عشرة مساكين، كل مسكين لا نصف صاع يزيد ولا ينقص. أما القيمة هنا تزيد وتنقص فيخير إن شاء تصدق به على مسكين وإن شاء صام يوماً كاملاً لأن الصوم أقل من يوم غير مشروع. وأشار إلى أن الواجب لو كان دون طعام مسكين بأن قتل يربوعاً أو عصفوراً فهو مخير أيضاً، وإلى أنه يجوز الجمع بين الصوم والإطعام بخلاف كفارة اليمين والفرق أن في كفارة الصيد الصوم أصل كالإطعام حتى يجوز الصوم مع القدرة على الإطعام فجاز الجمع بينهما وإكمال أحدهما بالآخر، وأما في كفارة اليمين فالصوم بدل عن التكفير بالمال حتى لا يجوز المصير إليه مع القدرة على المال فلا يجوز الجمع بين الأصل والبدل للتنافي . وشمل كلامه ما إذا كان هذا الفاضل من جنس ما فعله أولاً حتى لو اختار الهدي وفضل من القيمة ما لا يبلغ هدياً فهو مخير في الفضل أيضاً. وعلى هذا لو بلغت قيمته هديين إن شاء ذبحهما، وإن شاء تصدق بالطعام، وإن شاء صام عن كل نصف صاع يوماً، وإن شاء ذبح أحدهما وأطعم وصام بقي فيجمع بين الأنواع الثلاثة أو يتصدق بالقيمة من الدراهم أو الدنانير. وذكر الولوالجي في فتاواه أن المعتبر في الطعام قيمة الصيد، وفي الصوم قيمة الطعام، وهكذا في البدائع
He said: (If there remains less than half a sa') he gives it in charity or fasts one day. Because the obligation upon him is to consider the quantity and the number of poor; he was incapable of considering the quantity so it falls, and he is able to consider the number, so what he is able to do is binding upon him, unlike the kaffarah of an oath, because it is determined by feeding ten poor, each poor [receiving] no more and no less than half a sa'. As for the value here, it increases and decreases, so he is given a choice: if he wishes he gives it in charity to one poor, and if he wishes he fasts a full day, because fasting less than a day is not legislated. And he indicated that if the obligation were less than the food of one poor, such as if he killed a jerboa or a sparrow, then he is also given a choice. And that it is permitted to combine fasting and feeding, unlike the kaffarah of an oath. The difference is that in hunting kaffarah, fasting is an original [option] like feeding, so fasting is permitted even when able to feed, so combination is permitted and completing one with the other. As for oath kaffarah, fasting is a substitute for monetary expiation, so it is not permitted to resort to it while able to use money, so combination of original and substitute is not permitted due to inconsistency. And his speech includes the case where this excess is of the same type as what he did initially, so if he chose the sacrifice and from the value there remained what does not reach a sacrifice, then he is given a choice regarding the excess. Upon this, if its value reached two sacrifices, if he wishes he may slaughter both, if he wishes he may give charity with food, if he wishes he may fast a day for every half sa', if he wishes he may slaughter one, feed, and fast the rest, thus combining the three types, or he may give the value in dirhams or dinars. And al-Walwaliji mentioned in his Fatawa that what is considered in food is the value of the game, and in fasting the value of food, and likewise in al-Bada'i.
Source pages p. 56

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the matn's ruling regarding the kaffarah for hunting when a muhrim kills game and the compensation due exceeds the required amount, but the excess is less than half a sa'. The commentator explains the ruling and contrasts it with the kaffarah for a broken oath. The key point is that in hunting kaffarah, the obligation takes into account both the quantity (food) and the number of poor people. If the excess is less than half a sa', the muhrim cannot fulfill the quantity requirement for another poor person, so he has a choice: either give that excess as charity to one poor person, or fast one day. This differs from oath kaffarah where the amount is fixed at half a sa' per poor and no variation is allowed. The commentator also clarifies that combining fasting and feeding is permitted in hunting kaffarah because both are original options, whereas in oath kaffarah, fasting is only a substitute for feeding and cannot be combined with it. Further, the commentator extends the ruling to cases where the excess is even less than the food of one poor (e.g., killing a small animal like a jerboa), and also discusses scenarios where the muhrim chooses to sacrifice an animal (hady) instead. In that case, if the value exceeds the isafice of one hady, he has options: slaughter multiple, feed, fast, or combine. The commentator quotes al-Walwaliji and al-Bada'i stating that the value of food is assessed based on the game, and the value of fasting based on the food.

Key Terms
كفارة الصيد (kaffarat al-sayd): The compensation for a muhrim who kills game during ihram, which can be sacrifice, feeding, or fasting.
نصف صاع (nisaf sa'): Half a sa', a measure of volume approximately 1.5 liters, used here as the minimum unit for feeding a poor person.
صوم (sawm): Fasting as an alternative form of compensation in kaffarah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) He must fast two days
B) He must feed two poor people with half a sa' each
C) He may give the excess as charity to one poor person or fast one day
D) He must combine both charity and fasting

Key Takeaway
In hunting kaffarah, when the excess compensation is less than half a sa', the muhrim has the choice to give it as charity to one poor or fast one day, unlike the fixed nature of oath kaffarah.

Liability for Injuring Game in Ihram
Ruling on liability for injuring game with proof by analogy.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on compensation for injuring game and identify the qiyas principle that the part is considered like the whole.

Core Idea
Injuring game in ihram requires compensation for the loss, analogizing the part to the whole as in property rights.

The commentator explains that if a muhrim wounds game, cuts off a limb, or plucks feathers, he must compensate for the reduction in value. This ruling is derived through qiyas (analogy) from property rights, where injury to a part requires compensation proportional to the loss. This lesson focuses on the liability principle and its proof.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the ruling
The act is injuring game (wounding, cutting a limb, plucking feathers) while in ihram. The ruling is that the muhrim must compensate for the loss in value (daman ma naqas).
2
Examine the proof principle
The commentator states 'considering the part like the whole, as in the rights of servants' (i'tibar al-ba'd bi'l-kull). This is a qiyas: just as in property law, injury to part of an owned item requires compensation for the loss, so too for game.
This is an established Hanafi usul principle.
3
Note the implication of non-death
The passage contrasts wounding with the previous case of killing. If the animal had died from the wound, the ruling would be different (full kaffarah). Since it did not, only compensation for the loss is due.
This distinction is crucial: injury is treated differently from killing.
4
Acknowledge the intra-Hanafi dispute (contextual)
The commentator briefly mentions a disagreement among Abu Yusuf, Muhammad, and Abu Hanifa regarding kaffarat al-halaq (shaving hair), but clarifies that this dispute does not apply to hunting; there is consensus (bila khilaf) on the feeding method for hunting.
This is a tangential point; the core ruling on daman is agreed upon.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (وإن جرحه أو قطع عضوه أو نتف شعره ضمن ما نقص اعتباراً للبعض بالكل كما في حقوق العباد أفاد بمقابلة الجرح للقتل المتقدم أنه لم يمت من هذا الجرح لأنه لو مات منه عما أبي يوسف خلافاً لمحمد وعن أبي حنيفة روايتان والأصح أنه مع الأول لكن هذا الخلاف في كفارة الحلق من الأذى، وأما كفارة الصيد فيجوز الإطعام على وجه الإباحة بلا خلاف فيضع لهم طعاماً ويمكنهم منه حتى يستوفوا أكلتين مشبعتين غداء وعشاء، أو سحوراً وعشاء، أو غدائين أو عشاءين، لكن الأول أولى فإن غداهم لا غير أو عشاهم فقط لا يجزئه لكن إن غداهم وأعطاهم قيمة العشاء أو بالعكس جاز، والمستحب أن يكون مأدوماً، وفي الهداية لا بد من الإدام في خبز الشعير. وفي المصفى : غير البر لا يجوز إلا بإدام. وفي البدائع : يستوي كون الطعام مادوماً أو غير مأدوم حتى لو غداهم وعشاهم خبزاً بلا إدام أجزأه وكذا لو أطعم خبز الشعير أو سويقاً أو تمراً لأن ذلك قد يؤكل وحده. ثم المعتبر هو الشبع التام لا مقدار الطعام حتى لو قدم أربعة أرغفة أو ثلاثة بين يدي ستة مساكين وشبعوا أجزأه وإن لم يبلغ ذلك صاعاً أو نصف صاع ولو كان أحدهم شبعان قيل لا
He said: (And if he wounds it, or cuts off its limb, or plucks its feathers, he compensates for the loss) considering the part like the whole, as in the rights of servants. It indicates by contrasting wounding with the previous killing that it did not die from this wound, because if he had died from it, [there would be a difference] but from Abu Yusuf contrary to Muhammad, and from Abu Hanifa two narrations, and the most sound is that it is with the first. But this difference is in the kaffarah for shaving hair due to harm. As for the kaffarah for hunting, feeding is permitted on a permissive basis without disagreement: he places food for them and enables them to take it until they satisfy two full meals: lunch and dinner, or breakfast and dinner, or two lunches or two dinners, but the first is better. If he feeds them only lunch or only dinner, it does not suffice. However, if he feeds them lunch and gives them the value of dinner, or vice versa, it is permissible. It is recommended that it be with seasoning (idam). In al-Hidaya: there must be seasoning in barley bread. In al-Musaffa: other than wheat is not permissible except with seasoning. In al-Bada'i: it is equal whether the food is seasoned or not, so even if he feeds them lunch and dinner with plain bread without seasoning, it suffices. Likewise if he feeds barley bread, sawiq, or dates, because these are eaten alone. Then what is considered is complete satiation, not the quantity of food, so if he places four or three loaves before six poor people and they become full, it suffices even if that does not reach a sa' or half a sa'. And if one of them was already full, it is said no (it does not suffice).
Source pages p. 56

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the matn's ruling that if a muhrim injures game (e.g., cuts off a limb, plucks feathers), he is liable for the reduction in value, by analogy to the whole. The commentator notes that this implies the animal did not die from the injury; if it had, the ruling would be different. There is a brief mention of a disagreement among the early Hanafi imams (Abu Yusuf, Muhammad, Abu Hanifa) regarding the kaffarah for shaving hair (halaq) during ihram, but the commentator clarifies that this disagreement does not apply to hunting kaffarah; there is consensus (bila khilaf) that feeding is permissible in hunting kaffarah. The bulk of the passage then details the method of feeding: the muhrim must provide two satisfying meals (lunch and dinner, etc.), and the food must be such that the poor become fully satiated. There is a difference of opinion among Hanafi scholars regarding the necessity of seasoning (idam) with the bread, with al-Hidaya requiring it for barley bread, al-Musaffa requiring it for non-wheat grains, and al-Bada'i dispensing with the requirement altogether since bread alone can be eaten. The key rule is that satiation is the criterion, not a fixed quantity. Therefore, even if the amount of bread is less than a sa', it suffices if the poor are full. However, if one of the recipients was already full before being fed, it is said that it does not suffice.

Key Terms
ضمن ما نقص (damana ma naqas): He is liable for the amount of decrease in value caused by his action.
اعتبار البعض بالكل (i'tibar al-ba'd bi'l-kull): Considering the part like the whole: an analogy that the ruling for a part is the same as the ruling for the whole in terms of proportional liability.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the basis for the ruling that injury to game requires compensation?
A) A direct Quranic verse
B) Consensus of the Companions
C) Analogy (qiyas) considering the part like the whole
D) Istihsan

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, injuring game in ihram requires compensation for the loss by analogy to property rights; the part is treated like the whole.

Method of Feeding as Compensation for Hunting
Detailed rules for feeding as compensation for hunting.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi requirements for feeding as compensation for hunting, including the number of meals, the criterion of satiation, and the disagreement over seasoning.

Core Idea
Feeding for hunting kaffarah requires two full meals until satiation; quantity is not fixed, but the food's content is debated.

The passage details the method of it'am (feeding) for hunting kaffarah. There is consensus that feeding on a permissive basis is valid, but the number of meals, the need for seasoning, and the criterion of satiation are discussed. This lesson unpacks these rules and the intra-Hanafi disputes.

Guided Path
1
Identify the method of feeding
The muhrim must feed the poor on a permissive basis (wajh al-ibaha): he places food and allows them to eat until full.
No fixed amount is imposed.
2
Determine the number of meals
Two full meals are required: generally lunch and dinner (ghada' wa 'asha'). Alternatives like breakfast and dinner (sahur wa 'asha') or two lunches/two dinners also count.
The best is lunch and dinner.
3
Understand the criterion of satiation
The key is complete satiation (shiba' tamm), not a specific quantity. Even if the amount is less than a sa', it suffices if the recipients are full.
This is a unique Hanafi emphasis.
4
Explore the seasoning dispute
Al-Hidaya requires seasoning (idam) for barley bread. Al-Musaffa requires it for non-wheat grains. Al-Bada'i says no seasoning is needed; the food alone suffices.
The latter is the more lenient view.
5
Note the exception of an already full person
If one of the recipients was already full before being fed, it is said that the feeding does not count for that person, possibly requiring another recipient.
This is a cautionary point.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (وإن جرحه أو قطع عضوه أو نتف شعره ضمن ما نقص اعتباراً للبعض بالكل كما في حقوق العباد أفاد بمقابلة الجرح للقتل المتقدم أنه لم يمت من هذا الجرح لأنه لو مات منه عما أبي يوسف خلافاً لمحمد وعن أبي حنيفة روايتان والأصح أنه مع الأول لكن هذا الخلاف في كفارة الحلق من الأذى، وأما كفارة الصيد فيجوز الإطعام على وجه الإباحة بلا خلاف فيضع لهم طعاماً ويمكنهم منه حتى يستوفوا أكلتين مشبعتين غداء وعشاء، أو سحوراً وعشاء، أو غدائين أو عشاءين، لكن الأول أولى فإن غداهم لا غير أو عشاهم فقط لا يجزئه لكن إن غداهم وأعطاهم قيمة العشاء أو بالعكس جاز، والمستحب أن يكون مأدوماً، وفي الهداية لا بد من الإدام في خبز الشعير. وفي المصفى : غير البر لا يجوز إلا بإدام. وفي البدائع : يستوي كون الطعام مادوماً أو غير مأدوم حتى لو غداهم وعشاهم خبزاً بلا إدام أجزأه وكذا لو أطعم خبز الشعير أو سويقاً أو تمراً لأن ذلك قد يؤكل وحده. ثم المعتبر هو الشبع التام لا مقدار الطعام حتى لو قدم أربعة أرغفة أو ثلاثة بين يدي ستة مساكين وشبعوا أجزأه وإن لم يبلغ ذلك صاعاً أو نصف صاع ولو كان أحدهم شبعان قيل لا
He said: (And if he wounds it, or cuts off its limb, or plucks its feathers, he compensates for the loss) considering the part like the whole, as in the rights of servants. It indicates by contrasting wounding with the previous killing that it did not die from this wound, because if he had died from it, [there would be a difference] but from Abu Yusuf contrary to Muhammad, and from Abu Hanifa two narrations, and the most sound is that it is with the first. But this difference is in the kaffarah for shaving hair due to harm. As for the kaffarah for hunting, feeding is permitted on a permissive basis without disagreement: he places food for them and enables them to take it until they satisfy two full meals: lunch and dinner, or breakfast and dinner, or two lunches or two dinners, but the first is better. If he feeds them only lunch or only dinner, it does not suffice. However, if he feeds them lunch and gives them the value of dinner, or vice versa, it is permissible. It is recommended that it be with seasoning (idam). In al-Hidaya: there must be seasoning in barley bread. In al-Musaffa: other than wheat is not permissible except with seasoning. In al-Bada'i: it is equal whether the food is seasoned or not, so even if he feeds them lunch and dinner with plain bread without seasoning, it suffices. Likewise if he feeds barley bread, sawiq, or dates, because these are eaten alone. Then what is considered is complete satiation, not the quantity of food, so if he places four or three loaves before six poor people and they become full, it suffices even if that does not reach a sa' or half a sa'. And if one of them was already full, it is said no (it does not suffice).
Source pages p. 56

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the matn's ruling that if a muhrim injures game (e.g., cuts off a limb, plucks feathers), he is liable for the reduction in value, by analogy to the whole. The commentator notes that this implies the animal did not die from the injury; if it had, the ruling would be different. There is a brief mention of a disagreement among the early Hanafi imams (Abu Yusuf, Muhammad, Abu Hanifa) regarding the kaffarah for shaving hair (halaq) during ihram, but the commentator clarifies that this disagreement does not apply to hunting kaffarah; there is consensus (bila khilaf) that feeding is permissible in hunting kaffarah. The bulk of the passage then details the method of feeding: the muhrim must provide two satisfying meals (lunch and dinner, etc.), and the food must be such that the poor become fully satiated. There is a difference of opinion among Hanafi scholars regarding the necessity of seasoning (idam) with the bread, with al-Hidaya requiring it for barley bread, al-Musaffa requiring it for non-wheat grains, and al-Bada'i dispensing with the requirement altogether since bread alone can be eaten. The key rule is that satiation is the criterion, not a fixed quantity. Therefore, even if the amount of bread is less than a sa', it suffices if the poor are full. However, if one of the recipients was already full before being fed, it is said that it does not suffice.

Key Terms
الإطعام على وجه الإباحة (al-it'am 'ala wajh al-ibaha): Feeding on a permissive basis, meaning the muhrim places food and allows the poor to eat freely until they are full, without specifying a fixed quantity.
شبع (shiba'): Satiation; the condition of being full after eating.
إدام (idam): Seasoning or something to eat with bread, such as dates, meat, or vegetables.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the essential criterion for feeding as compensation for hunting?
A) A fixed amount of one sa' per person
B) Complete satiation of the recipients
C) The food must include meat
D) The feeding must be done at a specific time

Key Takeaway
Feeding for hunting kaffarah must result in full satiation of the poor through two meals; the quantity of food is secondary, and seasoning is debated.

Dispute on Game Compensation: Qiyas, Istihsan, and Tadakhul
Intra-Hanafi dispute on game penalty with qiyas, istihsan, and tadakhul.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi positions on compensation when a wounded game animal disappears or later dies, and apply the principle of tadakhul al-jinayatayn to determine the number of kaffarah due.

Core Idea
When a muhrim wounds game, istihsan overrides qiyas for full value on disappearance; if death follows before atonement, the acts merge into one.

This passage from Bahr al-Raiq delves into a subtle intra-Hanafi debate about the penalty (jaza') for a muhrim who wounds a game animal. The key tension is between strict analogy (qiyas) and juristic preference (istihsan) when the animal disappears, and further whether a subsequent killing before atonement merges with the initial wound or remains separate. Understanding this dispute sharpens your ability to trace how Hanafi masters reconcile conflicting principles within their school.

Guided Path
1
Distinguish the two scenarios
Identify that the passage covers two main cases: (1) the animal disappears after wounding, fate unknown, and (2) the animal is wounded and later dies (either before or after atonement). Each triggers different rulings.
The first scenario leads to the qiyas-istihsan debate; the second leads to the tadakhul debate.
2
Analyse the qiyas vs istihsan for disappearance
According to qiyas, the muhrim owes only the decrease in value at the time of injury, like owned property. Istihsan (preferred) imposes full value as a precaution, drawing an analogy to game captured from the Haram and released.
The text states 'al-istihsan an yalzimahu jami‘ al-qimah ihtiyāṭan'.
3
Examine the tadakhul dispute when death follows
If the muhrim wounds the animal and later kills it before atoning for the wound, some scholars (e.g., al-Hakim, Ibn al-Humam) hold that the two acts merge into one, so only one kaffarah is due. Others maintain separate liability.
The key term is 'tadakhul al-jinayatayn' (overlap of two injuries).
4
Identify the intra-Hanafi variant on regrowth of parts
Abu Hanifa rules no compensation if a lost part (tooth, feather, eye) regrows completely, while Abu Yusuf requires 'sadaqat al-alam' (charity for pain). This illustrates a deeper methodological difference.
The passage notes 'ind Abī Ḥanīfa lā shay‘ ‘alayh, wa ‘ind Abī Yūsuf ‘alayh ṣadaqat al-alam'.
5
Determine the mufta bihi position
Later authorities like Ibn al-Humam rely on the view from al-Bada'i that the two injuries merge, thus only one kaffarah. This is the relied-upon position for fatwa.
The commentator writes 'fa-huwa al-mu‘awwal' (so it is the relied-upon).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كمال القيمة، فإن غاب ولم يعلم موته ولا حياته فالقياس أن يضمن النقصان للشك في سبب الكمال كالصيد المملوك إذا جرحه وغاب والاستحسان أن يلزمه جميع القيمة احتياطاً كمن أخذ صيداً من الحرم ثم أرسله ولا يدري أدخل الحرم أم لا فإنه تجب قيمته لأن جزاء الصيد يسلك به مسلك العبادة من وجه كذا في المحيط وأطلق في ضمانه النقصان بسبب الجرح فشمل ما إذا برئ منه فإنه لا يسقط الجزاء ببرئه لأن الجزاء يجب بإتلاف جزء من الصيد وبالاندمال لا يتبين أن الإتلاف لم يكن بخلاف ما إذا جرح آدمياً فاندملت جراحته فلم يبق لها أثر أنه لا ضمان عليه لأن الضمان هناك إنما يجب لأجل الشين وقد ارتفع. كذا في البدائع، وفي المحيط خلافه فإنه قال : وإن بريء منه ولم يبق له أثر لا يضمن والظاهر الأول لما الضمان قد زال فيزول الضمان كما في الصيد المملوك ا هـ . سبب تقدم من الفرق بين جزاء الصيد والصيد المملوك في مسألة ما إذا غاب بعد الجرح، وعلى هذا لو قلع سن ظبي أو نتف ريش صيد فنبت أو ضرب عين صيد فابيضت ثم ذهب البياض فلا عليه عند أبي حنيفة، وعند أبي يوسف عليه صدقة الألم. وأشار بكون الجراحة جناية مستقلة إلى أنه لو صيداً فكفر ثم قتله كفر أخرى لأنهما جنايتان، وإلى أنه لو لم يكفر جرح حتى قتله لزمه كفارة بالقتل ونقصان بالجراحة كما في المحيط. وفي الولوالجية: لو جرح صيداً ثم كفر عنه ثم مات أجزأته الكفارة التي أداها لأنه أدى بعد وجود سبب الوجوب . وفي المحيط معزياً إلى الجامع : محرم بعمرة جرح صيداً جرحاً لا يستهلكه ثم أضاف إليها حجة ثم جرحه أيضاً فمات من الكل فعليه للعمرة قيمته صحيحاً وقيمته للحج وبه الجرح الأول، ولو حل من العمرة ثم أحرم بالحجة ثم جرحه الثانية فعليه للعمرة قيمته وبه الجرح شيء نقله ذلك قتله وجب كفارة يجوز، وإليه مال شمس الأئمة الحلواني كذا في اللباب وشرحه قوله : (والظاهر الأول) قال في الشرنبلالية : يعني الظاهر بالنسبة لما حصل عنده لا أنه ظاهر الرواية ولذا قال في النهر : إن كلام البدائع هو المناسب للإطلاق قوله : لزمه كفارة بالقتل ونقصان بالجراحة قال في شرح اللباب بعد منسك الطرابلسي، وفي الفتح ولو جرح صيداً ولم يكفر حتى عن واحدة وما نقصته الجراحة الأولى ساقط وكذا قال في البدائع وليس عليه للجراحة شيء لأنه لما قتله قبل أن يكفر عن الجراحة صار كأنه قتله دفعة واحدة. وذكر الحاكم في مختصره إلا ما نقصته الجراحة الأولى أي يلزمه ضمان صيد مجروح لأن ذلك الزمان قد وجب عليه مرة فلا يجب عليه مرة أخرى ا هـ. وحاصله تداخل الجنايتين ومآله إلى جناية واحدة كما حققه ابن الهمام تبعاً لما في البدائع فهو المعول فتدبر وتأمل ا هـ . وكذا مشى عليه في متن اللباب لكن ما ذكره الحاكم يفيد التوفيق بأن من أوجب نقصان الجراحة أوجب قيمته في القتل مجروحاً، ومن لم يوجبها أوجب قيمته في القتل سالماً والمال فيهما واحد فتأمل قوله : (ثم كفر عنه أي كفارة الموت كما في النهر قوله: (وانتقصت قيمته أو ازدادت أي قيمة جنسه لا خصوص هذا المضروب إذ لا يمكن زيادة قيمته بعد الضرب
[The ruling on] full value: if it disappears and its death or life is unknown, the qiyas is that he compensates for the decrease due to doubt about the cause of completeness, like owned game if he wounds it and it disappears. The istihsan is that he is liable for the entire value as a precaution, like one who takes game from the Haram and then releases it and does not know whether it entered the Haram or not, for its value is obligatory because the penalty for game follows the path of worship in one sense, as in al-Muhit. And he [the author] made absolute in his liability for the decrease due to the wound, so it includes [the case] if he [the animal] recovers from it, for the penalty does not fall due to recovery, because the penalty is due for destroying a part of the game, and by healing it does not become clear that the destruction did not occur, unlike if he wounds a human and his wounds heal and no trace remains: there is no liability, because liability there is only due to the defect and it has disappeared. Thus in al-Bada'i, and in al-Muhit there is a contrary view: he said if he recovers from it and no trace remains, he is not liable, and the first is the apparent [view] because liability has ceased, so liability ceases as in owned game. End. The reason is a prior difference between the penalty for game and owned game in the matter of when it disappears after wounding. Upon this, if he extracts a tooth of a gazelle or plucks feathers that then regrow, or strikes the eye of a game animal so it becomes white and then the whiteness goes, then according to Abu Hanifa there is nothing on him; according to Abu Yusuf there is the charity of pain upon him. And he [the author] indicated that the wound being an independent injury implies that if he kills game and then atones, then kills it again, he owes another atonement because they are two injuries. And that if he did not atone for the wound until he killed it, he owes a kaffarah for the killing and a decrease for the wound, as in al-Muhit. In al-Walwaljiyya: if he wounds a game animal and then atones for it, then it dies, the atonement he performed suffices because he performed it after the cause of obligation existed. In al-Muhit, attributed to al-Jami': a muhrim in 'umrah wounds a game animal with a wound that does not render it unsalable, then adds hajj to it [i.e., joins hajj to 'umrah], then wounds it again, and it dies from both, so for the 'umrah he owes its full value [as a healthy animal], and for the hajj he owes its value with the first wound. And if he ended 'umrah then entered ihram for hajj and then wounded it a second time, for the 'umrah he owes its value and for the wound... something transmitted that he killed, a kaffarah is obligatory, permissible, and Shams al-A'imma al-Halwani inclined to it, as in al-Lubab and its commentary. His saying: (al-Zahir al-awwal): in al-Shurnbalaliyya: meaning the apparent in relation to what he has acquired, not that it is the apparent of the transmission. Hence in al-Nahr: the statement of al-Bada'i is more appropriate for absolute expression. His saying: he owes a kaffarah for the killing and a decrease for the wound: in Sharh al-Lubab after the Manasik of al-Tarabulusi, and in al-Fath: if he wounds a game animal and does not atone until [he kills it]... and what was decreased by the first wound is dropped, and likewise in al-Bada'i: there is nothing on him for the wound because when he killed it before atoning for the wound, it becomes as if he killed it all at once. And al-Hakim mentioned in his Mukhtasar: except what was decreased by the first wound, i.e., he owes the compensation of a wounded game animal because that was obligatory once, so it does not become obligatory again. End. The summary is the overlap of the two injuries and their outcome is one injury, as verified by Ibn al-Humam following what is in al-Bada'i, so it is the relied-upon. So consider and reflect. End. And similarly he proceeded upon it in the text of al-Lubab, but what al-Hakim mentioned indicates reconciliation: that whoever required the decrease for the wound required its value in the killing as wounded, and whoever did not require it required its value in the killing as sound, and the property in both is one. So consider. His saying: (Then he atoned for it, i.e., the kaffarah of death as in al-Nahr. His saying: (and its value decreased or increased), i.e., the value of its species, not particularly this struck one, because its value cannot increase after striking.
Source pages p. 57

Commentary
This passage is a detailed discussion of the Hanafi positions on the compensation for a muhrim who injures a game animal that later disappears or dies. The commentator presents a qiyas (analogy) and an istihsan (juristic preference) when the animal's fate is unknown: qiyas would require only the decrease in value at the time of injury, likening it to owned property that is lost after injury; istihsan (preferred) requires full value as a precaution, drawing an analogy to releasing a captured game from the Haram. The text then addresses the scenario where the animal recovers completely from the injury: according to al-Bada'i, the penalty remains because it was incurred for destroying a part, while al-Muhit contradicts this, stating that if no trace remains, no compensation is due. The commentator suggests the first view is more apparent. This discussion is connected to the difference between the penalty for game (which is like a religious obligation) and owned property. The passage also covers disputes between Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf regarding compensation when lost parts regrow (e.g., tooth, feather, eye). Furthermore, it explores the consequences of multiple ihrams (umrah and hajj) and whether two compensations are due when a muhrim injures an animal and later kills it after atoning for the injury, or kills it without having atoned. There is a divergence: some scholars hold that two compensations are due (one for injury, one for killing), while others consider them overlapping such that only one compensation is due, essentially merging the two into a single act. The preferred view (mu'tamad) according to later scholars like Ibn al-Humam is that they overlap into one injury, thus only one kaffarah is required. The commentator ends with a note that the value considered is of the species, not the particular animal struck, because the value cannot increase after being struck.

Key Terms
القياس (al-qiyas): Analogical reasoning: in this context, comparing the case of an injured game animal that disappears to owned property, requiring only the loss in value.
الاستحسان (al-istihsan): Juristic preference: preferring full compensation as a precaution due to the religious nature of the penalty for game.
تداخل الجنايتين (tadakhul al-jinayatayn): The overlapping of two injuries, resulting in a single legal consequence.
جزاء الصيد (jaza' al-sayd): The penalty for hunting or injuring game while in ihram.
صدقة الألم (sadaqat al-alam): Charity for pain: a compensation for the inflicted pain even if the physical loss is later restored.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon Hanafi position (mu'tamad), when a muhrim wounds a game animal and then kills it before atoning, how many kaffarah are due?
A) Two: one for the wound and one for the killing
B) One: the acts merge into a single continuous act
C) Only the decrease in value for the wound, no kaffarah
D) One kaffarah plus an additional charity for pain

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, when a muhrim's wounding of game is followed by killing before atonement, the two acts are treated as one, resulting in a single kaffarah.

Wounding Game and Its Disappearance: Qiyas vs Istihsan
Explains the ruling when a muhrim wounds game that disappears.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rule that when a muhrim wounds game that disappears, full value is wajib by istihsan, and distinguish this from the qiyas ruling of only guaranteeing the decrease.

Core Idea
When game disappears after being wounded, istihsan requires full value as a precaution because the penalty is treated like worship.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq explains a nuanced ruling: if a muhrim wounds game and it disappears, what compensation is due? Pure analogy (qiyas) would require only the decrease, but the Hanafi school applies istihsan (juristic preference) to require the full value. Understanding why istihsan overrides qiyas here is key to mastering Hanafi methodology in ibadat-related compensations.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is a muhrim (pilgrim in ihram) wounding game that then disappears. The ruling by istihsan is wajib to pay the full value.
If the game is killed outright, full value is wajib by consensus. The dispute arises only when death is uncertain.
2
Recognize the two possible rulings
By pure qiyas (analogy to owned game), the muhrim would only guarantee the decrease in value caused by the wound. By istihsan, he pays the full value.
The qiyas is based on the doubt in the cause of completeness (shakk fi sabab al-kamal).
3
Understand the illa for qiyas
The illa (effective cause) is the lack of knowledge of death. In owned game, the owner guarantees only the decrease because there is doubt about survival. The same doubt applies here by qiyas.
4
Understand the basis for istihsan
Istihsan overrides qiyas because jaza' al-sayd (penalty for hunting) is treated like an act of worship (maslak al-ibadah). Acts of worship require precaution (ihtiyat) in cases of doubt.
The parallel is someone who takes game from the Haram and releases it without knowing if it re-entered: full value is wajib.
5
Apply the same reasoning to analogous cases
The principle applies whenever the penalty resembles worship: uncertainty triggers the stricter obligation to ensure full compensation.
This shows how istihsan functions as a secondary source in Hanafi usul.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فصل إن قتل محرم صيداً وجب كمال القيمة، فإن غاب ولم يعلم موته ولا حياته فالقياس أن يضمن النقصان للشك في سبب الكمال كالصيد المملوك إذا جرحه وغاب والاستحسان أن يلزمه جميع القيمة احتياطاً كمن أخذ صيداً من الحرم ثم أرسله ولا يدري أدخل الحرم أم لا فإنه تجب قيمته لأن جزاء الصيد يسلك به مسلك العبادة من وجه كذا في المحيط
Chapter: If a muhrim kills game, the full value is obligatory. If it disappears and its death or life is unknown, then by analogy he guarantees the decrease due to doubt in the cause of completeness, like owned game if he wounds it and it disappears; and by juristic preference (istihsan) he is obligated to pay the entire value as a precaution, like one who takes game from the Haram then releases it and does not know whether it entered the Haram or not, then its value is obligatory because the penalty for game is treated like an act of worship in some respects, as in al-Muhit.
Source pages p. 57

Commentary
This passage presents a ruling on a muhrim who wounds game that then disappears, with unknown fate. The author states that if a muhrim kills game, he must pay the full value. Then he discusses the case where the game disappears after being wounded, and its death or life is unknown. By pure analogy (qiyas), the muhrim would only guarantee the decrease in value caused by the wound, because the full value is only certain if death is confirmed. However, by istihsan (juristic preference), he must pay the full value as a precautionary measure, because the penalty for hunting (jaza' al-sayd) is treated like an act of worship in requiring precaution. The author draws a parallel to someone who takes game from the Haram and releases it without knowing if it re-entered; in that case, full value is also required. The istihsan is based on the principle that when in doubt about the completion of a religious obligation, one takes the more cautious route.

Key Terms
جزاء الصيد (jaza' al-sayd): The penalty or compensation owed by a muhrim for hunting game in the state of ihram
القياس (al-qiyas): The analogy that would lead to a ruling based on the effective cause ('illa) of doubt
الاستحسان (al-istihsan): Juristic preference that gives full value as a precaution due to the nature of the penalty as an act of worship

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, if a muhrim wounds game and it disappears without knowledge of its death, what is the ruling by istihsan?
A) Only the decrease in value is owed
B) Full value is owed as a precaution
C) No compensation is owed
D) It depends on the type of game

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, when a muhrim wounds game that disappears, the obligation to pay full value is established by istihsan due to the nature of the penalty as an act of worship, overriding the qiyas that would only guarantee the decrease.

Does a Healed Wound Remove the Penalty? Abu Hanifa vs Abu Yusuf
Discusses whether a wound that heals removes the penalty

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi position on whether a wound on game that heals removes the penalty, and distinguish the views of Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf regarding regeneration of body parts.

Core Idea
The penalty for wounding game is not removed by healing because the act of injury itself is the cause, unlike human injuries.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq discusses a key distinction between injuries to game and injuries to humans. While a healed human wound with no trace removes liability, the same is not true for game. However, there is an intra-Hanafi dispute when the injured part regenerates (e.g., tooth or feather regrows). Abu Hanifa holds no penalty, while Abu Yusuf imposes sadaqat al-alam (charity for pain). We will examine the reasoning behind each view.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position on healed wounds
Identify the general rule: a wound on game incurs a penalty regardless of healing, because the penalty is for the act of destroying a part, not for the lasting blemish.
This is from al-Bada'i' as the author's preferred view.
2
Analyze the qiyas with human injuries
Contrast with human injuries: if a human's wound heals without trace, no compensation because liability is for the blemish (shayn) which disappeared.
This distinction is crucial for understanding the different rationales.
3
Identify the exception for regenerated parts
Note that when a part (tooth, feather, eye) regrows, Abu Hanifa says no penalty because restoration negates the destruction. Abu Yusuf says a penalty for pain (sadaqat al-alam) remains.
This is the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf highlighted in the text.
4
Contrast Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf
Abu Hanifa focuses on the material restoration; Abu Yusuf focuses on the pain caused by the initial injury. Understand each imam's legal reasoning (talil).
The text mentions this ikhtilaf without explicit tarjih, but Abu Hanifa's view is mufta bihi.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
The relied-upon position for fatwa is Abu Hanifa's: no penalty if the part regrows. For wounds that heal without regeneration, the penalty remains.
This is based on the author's presentation and later Hanafi practice.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأطلق في ضمانه النقصان بسبب الجرح فشمل ما إذا برئ منه فإنه لا يسقط الجزاء ببرئه لأن الجزاء يجب بإتلاف جزء من الصيد وبالاندمال لا يتبين أن الإتلاف لم يكن بخلاف ما إذا جرح آدمياً فاندملت جراحته فلم يبق لها أثر أنه لا ضمان عليه لأن الضمان هناك إنما يجب لأجل الشين وقد ارتفع. كذا في البدائع، وفي المحيط خلافه فإنه قال : وإن بريء منه ولم يبق له أثر لا يضمن والظاهر الأول لما الضمان قد زال فيزول الضمان كما في الصيد المملوك ا هـ . سبب تقدم من الفرق بين جزاء الصيد والصيد المملوك في مسألة ما إذا غاب بعد الجرح، وعلى هذا لو قلع سن ظبي أو نتف ريش صيد فنبت أو ضرب عين صيد فابيضت ثم ذهب البياض فلا عليه عند أبي حنيفة، وعند أبي يوسف عليه صدقة الألم.
And he (the author) generalised in guaranteeing the decrease due to the wound, so it includes the case where it heals, for the penalty does not drop due to healing because the penalty is obligatory for destroying a part of the game, and by healing it is not known that the destruction did not occur, unlike wounding a human: if his wound heals and no trace remains, there is no liability because liability there is only for the blemish and it has disappeared. Thus in al-Bada'i'. In al-Muhit, it is the opposite: he said: if it heals and no trace remains, he does not guarantee. And the first is apparent because the penalty has been incurred, so the liability is removed, as in owned game. This is the basis for the difference between the penalty for game and owned game in the issue of disappearance after wounding. And on this, if he cuts a tooth of a gazelle or plucks a feather of game and it grows back, or strikes the eye of game and it becomes white then the whiteness goes away, then according to Abu Hanifa there is nothing on him, and according to Abu Yusuf there is a charity of pain (sadaqat al-alam).
Source pages p. 57

Commentary
This passage addresses the effect of a wound that heals without trace. The general principle in Hanafi fiqh is that a wound inflicted on game incurs a penalty because it causes loss of a part of the animal. Even if the wound heals completely, the penalty does not drop because the act of injury itself is the basis for the obligation, not the lasting effect. This is contrasted with injuring a human: if a human's wound heals without any blemish, there is no compensation because compensation for humans is for the blemish (shayn) which has disappeared. However, for game, the penalty is for the act of injuring a part, which cannot be undone. There is a dispute: In al-Bada'i', it is stated that the penalty remains even after healing. In al-Muhit, it is stated that if no trace remains, there is no penalty. The author sides with the first view. Then the passage applies this to cutting a tooth or plucking a feather that regrows. According to Abu Hanifa, there is no penalty because the part was restored. According to Abu Yusuf, there is a penalty for the pain (sadaqat al-alam). This shows an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf.

Key Terms
صدقة الألم (sadaqat al-alam): A compensatory payment for the pain caused by the injury, even if the wound heals
الشين (al-shayn): The blemish or disfigurement from a wound that is the basis for compensation in humans

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Hanifa, if a muhrim plucks a feather from game and it grows back, what is the ruling?
A) He must pay the full value of the game
B) He must pay sadaqat al-alam
C) There is no penalty because the feather regrew
D) He must pay the decrease in value

Key Takeaway
The penalty for wounding game remains even if the wound heals, but if a part regrows, Abu Hanifa's view (no penalty) is the relied-upon position.

Independent Offences: Wounding and Killing Game
Explains the independence of wounding and killing game and the rule of merging.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rule that wounding and killing game during ihram are separate offences and determine whether the expiations merge based on the timing of expiation.

Core Idea
Wounding and killing game are separate offences; they merge only if the muhrim fails to expiate for the wound before the animal dies.

When a muhrim harms game, each distinct act of injury is an independent crime. This lesson examines a common scenario: wounding the animal, then later killing it. The key question is whether the expiation for the wound and the expiation for the killing merge into one or remain separate. The ruling depends on whether the muhrim already expiated for the wound before the animal died.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two acts of harm
Determine the two separate acts: the wound (جراحة) and the kill (قتل). They occur at different times and each is a jinayah (offence).
The text explicitly says 'innahuma jinaayatani' (they are two crimes).
2
Check whether expiation for the wound was performed before the kill
If the muhrim gave expiation for the wound before killing the animal, the offences stay separate: a new expiation is due for the kill. If he did not expiate, the two offences merge (tadakhul) and only the killing expiation is required, but with an adjustment for the wound's effect on the value.
The text says: 'law lam yukaffir jarha hatta qatalahu lazimahu kaffaratun bi al-qatl wa nuqsanun bi al-jarahah' – if he didn't expiate the wound until he killed it, he owes expiation for killing and a decrease for the wound.
3
Apply the principle to multi‑ihram scenarios
The text also covers a case where the muhrim is in 'Umrah, wounds the animal, then adds Hajj, then wounds again and the animal dies. The ruling distinguishes based on whether he exited 'Umrah before the second wound. This shows the independent nature of each jinayah in relation to each ihram.
The detailed calculations in al‑Muhit and al‑Walwajiyya illustrate the complexity.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأشار بكون الجراحة جناية مستقلة إلى أنه لو صيداً فكفر ثم قتله كفر أخرى لأنهما جنايتان، وإلى أنه لو لم يكفر جرح حتى قتله لزمه كفارة بالقتل ونقصان بالجراحة كما في المحيط. وفي الولوالجية: لو جرح صيداً ثم كفر عنه ثم مات أجزأته الكفارة التي أداها لأنه أدى بعد وجود سبب الوجوب . وفي المحيط معزياً إلى الجامع : محرم بعمرة جرح صيداً جرحاً لا يستهلكه ثم أضاف إليها حجة ثم جرحه أيضاً فمات من الكل فعليه للعمرة قيمته صحيحاً وقيمته للحج وبه الجرح الأول، ولو حل من العمرة ثم أحرم بالحجة ثم جرحه الثانية فعليه للعمرة قيمته وبه الجرح
And he indicated that wounding is an independent crime: if he [..] then expiates then kills it, he expiates another because they are two crimes; and if he does not expiate the wound until he kills it, he incurs expiation for the killing and a decrease for the wound, as in al-Muhit. And in al-Walwajiyya: if he wounds game then expiates for it, then it dies, the expiation he performed suffices because he performed it after the cause of obligation existed. And in al-Muhit, attributed to al-Jami': a muhrim in 'Umrah wounds game with a non-lethal wound, then adds Hajj to it, then wounds it again and it dies from all, then he owes for the 'Umrah its full value and for Hajj its value and with it the first wound. And if he exited from 'Umrah then entered Ihram for Hajj then wounded it a second time, then he owes for 'Umrah its value and with it the wound.
Source pages p. 57

Commentary
This passage deals with the scenario where a muhrim commits multiple injuries on the same game. The key principle is that wounding and killing are two separate offences (jinaayatani). If the muhrim wounds the game, then expiates for that wound, and then later kills the same game, he must expiate again for the killing because it is a new offence. However, if he did not expiate for the wound before the animal died, and the death results from both the wound and the final blow, then the expiation for the killing covers the entire loss, and the decrease from the wound is not separately owed because the two offences merge into one when death occurs before expiation. The text gives examples from al-Walwajiyya and al-Muhit: If a muhrim in 'Umrah wounds game, then adds Hajj to his intention, then wounds again and the animal dies, he owes a full value for 'Umrah and a separate full value for Hajj, along with the first wound (meaning the value of the game in that state). If he exited 'Umrah before the second wound, then the calculation differs. The ruling is based on the nature of the offences as independent.

Key Terms
جناية مستقلة (jinayah mustaqillah): An independent crime; each injury to game is considered a separate offence for which a separate penalty is due
تداخل الجنايتين (tadakhul al-jinayatayn): The merging of two offences into one, such that only one penalty is due

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a muhrim wounds a game animal, then expiates for that wound, and then kills the same animal, what is the ruling?
A) Only one expiation is required because it is the same animal
B) He must expiate again for the killing because it is a separate offence
C) No expiation is required because the wound expiation covers everything
D) He must expiate for the wound again

Key Takeaway
Wounding and killing game during ihram are separate offences; they merge only when the muhrim fails to expiate for the wound before the animal dies.

Compensation for Partial Destruction of Game (Feathers, Limbs, Milk, Eggs)
Penalties for partial destruction of game during ihram.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rulings for various acts of partially destroying game during ihram and explain the legal reasoning behind each penalty.

Core Idea
Partial destruction of game can equate to killing: feathers and limbs are means of escape, and eggs have the potential to become game.

During ihram, a muhrim must avoid harming game. But what if he only plucks a feather, cuts a leg, milks, or breaks an egg? The Hanafi school provides detailed rulings for these partial destructions, treating some as equivalent to killing and others as requiring compensation based on the potential (urdiyya) of the egg. This lesson unpacks these rulings and their proofs.

Guided Path
1
Identify the acts and general principle
The passage covers five acts: plucking feathers, cutting limbs, milking, breaking eggs, and a dead chick emerging. The general principle is that compensation is wajib for each, but the amount varies.
2
Understand the reasoning for feathers and limbs
Feathers and limbs are called 'alat al-imtina'' (means of defence). Destroying them renders the animal defenceless, analogous to killing, so full value of the animal is due.
3
Analyze the ruling for milking
Milk is part of the animal, so compensation is due. There is an intra-Hanafi dispute: some say value of milk, others say decrease in the animal's value. The preferred view reconciles based on who consumes the milk.
4
Examine the rulings for eggs
An egg is the origin of the game and has 'urdiyya' (potential) to become game. By analogy, it is treated as game, so the value of the egg is due. If a dead chick emerges, istihsan overrides analogy: the egg was prepared for a live chick, so the value of a live chick is due.
5
Note the exception for rotten eggs
Only fresh eggs have potential. Rotten eggs lack urdiyya, so no penalty. This refutes the position that the shell value matters.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (وتجب القيمة بنتف ريشه وقطع قوائمه وحلبه وكسر بيضه وخروج فرخ ميت به أما نتف ريشه وقطع قوائمه فلأنه فوّت عليه الأمن بتفويت آلة الامتناع فصار كأنه قتله فلزمه قيمة كاملة، وأما حلبه فلأن اللبن من أجزائه فيكون معتبراً بكله فيجب عليه ضمان ما وهو قيمة اللبن، وأما كسر بيضه فلأنه أصل الصيد وله عرضية أن يصير صيداً فنزل منزلة الصيد احتياطاً وهو مروي عن علي وابن عباس رضي الله عنهما فوجب عليه قيمة البيض، وأما إذا خرج فرخ ميت بسبب الكسر فالقياس أن لا يغرم سوى قيمة البيضة لأن حياة الفرخ غير معلوم وجه الاستحسان أن البيض معد ليخرج منه الفرخ الحي والكسر قبل أوانه سبب لموته فيحال به عليه احتياطاً فتجب قيمته حياً كما صرح به. والريش جمع الريشة وهو الجناح، والقوائم الأرجل، وأطلق في كسر بيضه . وقيده في الهداية بأن لا يكون فاسداً لأنه لو كسر بيضة مذرة لا شيء عليه لأن ضمانها ليس لذاتها بل لعرضية الصيد وهو مفقود في الفاسدة، وبهذا انتفى قول الكرماني : إذا كسر بيضة نعامة مذرة وجب الجزاء لأن لقشرها قيمة، وإن كانت غيرها نعامة لا يجب شيء، وذلك لأن المحرم بالإحرام ليس منهياً عن التعرض للقشر بل للصيد فقط وليس للمذرة عرضية الصيدية كذا في فتح القدير. وفي البدائع : ولو شوى بيضاً أو جراداً فضمنه لا يحرم أكله، ولو أكله أو غيره حلالاً كان أو : (تأمل. أو المراد زادت قيمة شعره أو بدنه كما يأتي عن المحيط عند قوله ويذبح الحلال صيد الحرم». قوله : (وهو قيمة اللبن) هذا على ما في البحر الزاخر. وفي البدائع عليه ما نقصه الحلب كما لو أتلف جزءاً من أجزائه. وقد جمع الطرابلسي بين الروايتين حيث قال : وإذا حلب صيداً فعليه ما نقصه وقيمة ولعله محمول على ما إذا شربه بنفسه بخلاف ما إذا أطعمه الفقراء. كذا في شرح اللباب قوله : (وأما إذا خرج فرخ ميت الخ قال في العناية : هذه المسألة لا تخلو من أن علم أنه كان حياً ومات بالكسر أو علم أنه كان ميتاً أو لم يعلم أن موته بسبب الكسر أو لا ؛ فإن كان الأول ضمن قيمته، وإن كان الثاني فلا شيء عليه وإن كان الثالث فالقياس أن لا يغرم سوى قيمة البيضة الخ.
His statement: (And the value is obligatory for plucking its feathers, cutting its limbs, milking it, breaking its eggs, and a dead chick coming out from it) As for plucking its feathers and cutting its limbs, because he has caused it to lose security by destroying its means of defence, so it is as if he killed it, so he must pay a complete value. As for milking it, because the milk is part of its parts, so it is considered as a whole, so he must guarantee what he destroyed, which is the value of the milk. As for breaking its eggs, because the egg is the origin of the game and has the potential to become game, so it is treated as game precautionarily, and this is narrated from Ali and Ibn Abbas (may Allah be pleased with them), so he must pay the value of the egg. As for if a dead chick comes out due to the break, by analogy he does not owe more than the value of the egg because the life of the chick is unknown; the basis of istihsan is that the egg is prepared for a live chick to emerge, and breaking it before its time is the cause of its death, so it is attributed to him as a precaution, so he must pay its value alive as explicitly stated. And al-reesh is the plural of reesha, which is the wing, and al-qawa'im are the legs. And he gave an unrestricted ruling in breaking its eggs, but he restricted it in al-Hidayah to not being spoiled, because if he breaks a rotten egg, there is nothing on him because its guarantee is not for its essence but for the potential of game, which is absent in the rotten. And by this, the statement of al-Kirmani is refuted: if he breaks a rotten ostrich egg, the penalty is due because its shell has value, and if it is not an ostrich egg, nothing is due, because the muhrim is not prohibited from affecting the shell but only game, and the rotten has no potential of being game. Similarly in Fath al-Qadir. And in al-Bada'i': if he cooks eggs or locusts and is liable, it is not prohibited to eat them; if he eats them or someone else, halal or […].
Source pages p. 58

Commentary
This passage explains the penalties for various acts of partial destruction of game. Plucking feathers and cutting limbs incur full value because these acts deprive the animal of its ability to escape, effectively equating to killing it. Milking the game requires compensation for the value of the milk taken, but there is a variant: some say the decrease in value of the animal due to milking, while others say the value of the milk. The preferred view is that if the muhrim drinks the milk himself, he must pay the value of the milk; if he gives it to the poor, he pays the decrease. Breaking eggs: an egg is the origin of the game and has the potential (urdiyya) to become game, so it is treated like the game itself, and the penalty is the value of the egg. This is based on a narration from Ali and Ibn Abbas. If a dead chick emerges, by analogy only the egg's value is due, but by istihsan, the full value of a live chick is due because the break caused its death. The ruling applies only to fresh (non-rotten) eggs; rotten eggs have no potential to become game, so no penalty. The passage also mentions other details like cooking eggs, etc.

Key Terms
العرضية (al-urdiyya): The potential or capacity to become game; an egg has the potential to hatch into a game bird
آلة الامتناع (alat al-imtina'): The means of protection or defence, such as feathers and legs used by game to escape predators

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a muhrim breaks a rotten egg of a game bird, according to the Hanafi school, what is the ruling?
A) He must pay the full value of a live bird
B) He must pay the value of a fresh egg
C) There is no penalty because the egg is rotten and has no potential
D) He must pay the value of the shell

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, partial destruction of game during ihram incurs compensation through the principles of alat al-imtina' and urdiyya.

Animals a Muhrim May Kill Without Penalty
Lists animals that a muhrim may kill without penalty

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to list the seven animals a muhrim may kill without penalty and state the ruling.

Core Idea
A muhrim may kill harmful predatory animals without compensatory penalty.

While in the state of ihram, hunting game is prohibited. However, the Shari'ah makes an exception for certain harmful animals. This lesson presents the specific list from the Hanafi school, helping you distinguish between permissible and prohibited killing during hajj or umrah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is killing specific animals. The ruling is that no penalty (something) is incurred.
The word 'لا شيء' indicates complete exemption from compensation.
2
Memorize the list of animals
The passage enumerates seven distinct animals. Commit them to memory: crow, kite, wolf, snake, scorpion, mouse, and dog.
These are all considered inherently harmful or filthy.
3
Understand the underlying principle
The exception is based on harmfulness. Game animals are protected; harmful creatures are not. This principle helps extend the ruling to similar existing or new cases.
The list is exhaustive in the text but the principle can be analogized.
4
Apply the ruling to other scenarios
If you encounter an animal not listed but equally harmful (e.g., a rabid fox), apply qiyas (analogy) to determine if killing is permitted.
Consult reliable scholars for animals not explicitly mentioned.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
و لا شيء بقتل غراب وحدأة وذئب وحية وعقرب وفأرة وكلب
And nothing is incurred for killing a crow, a kite, a wolf, a snake, a scorpion, a mouse, and a dog.
Source pages p. 58

Commentary
This passage presents a concise list of animals that a muhrim may kill without incurring any penalty. These animals are generally considered harmful or predatory. The ruling is based on the principle that the prohibition of hunting for a muhrim applies to game animals, not to harmful creatures that pose a threat or are unclean. The animals listed include: crow (ghurab), kite (hida'ah), wolf (dhi'b), snake (hayyah), scorpion ('aqrab), mouse (fa'rah), and dog (kalb). This is a standard ruling in Hanafi fiqh. The listing is exhaustive for these types; other animals not mentioned may still be subject to the general prohibition.

Key Terms
محرم (muhrim): A person in the state of ihram for hajj or umrah.
غراب (ghurab): Crow, a black bird often considered harmful or filthy.
كلب (kalb): Dog, considered impure in Hanafi fiqh.

Compensation for Killing Game in Multiple Ihrams
Ruling on a muhrim in two ihrams killing game

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rule for compensating game killed by a muhrim in multiple ihrams, distinguishing between wounding and destruction and considering the effect of qiran.

Core Idea
Compensation for game in multiple ihrams is not simply additive; the type of injury and the sequence affect the amount.

In this lesson, we examine a specific scenario from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq: a muhrim who performs qiran after exiting Umrah and then wounds game. The ruling clarifies how many values must be paid and how the first and second wounds are assigned to each ihram. Understanding this nuance is essential for correctly applying the penalty (jaza) for violating ihram prohibitions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario
A muhrim first enters ihram for Umrah, then after completing it enters ihram for Hajj as qiran (combining Umrah and Hajj). While in the Hajj ihram, he wounds game, and the game later dies. Determine which ihram is liable for which wound.
2
Distinguish between wounding (jarh) and destruction (istihlak)
If the first wound (in Umrah) was just a wound and the game died from the second wound (in Hajj), the compensation is one value for Umrah and two values for qiran. If the first wound killed the game outright (destruction), then the compensation is full value for Umrah and two values for qiran.
The word 'istihlak' indicates total consumption/destruction.
3
Apply the value fluctuation rule
If the game's value changes between the time of wounding and death, the mufta bihi position (al-Kirmani) is to pay the greater of the two values.
This ensures the penalty is not diminished by a change in value.
4
Confirm the total compensation
Summarize: for a wound that leads to death, the compensation is 1 (Umrah) + 2 (qiran) = 3 values? Actually careful: It is one value for Umrah and two values for qiran, total three values. But if the first wound was destruction, it's also one value for Umrah and two for qiran, but the wording might be different. The text says 'gharima lil-ihram al-awwal qimatahu sahihan wa lil-qiran qimatayn' meaning he pays for the first ihram its value as sound (i.e., full value) and for qiran two values. So total also three values. The difference is that in the wounding case, the value for Umrah is only one value, but it's the value at the time of the second wound? The text: 'damin lil-umra al-qima wa bihi al-jarh al-thani' - it seems the value for Umrah is assigned to the second wound, and for qiran two values assigned to the first wound. The key nuance is that the first wound (in Umrah) is considered the cause for qiran's liability because the game died from the second wound, but the first wound still triggers liability for qiran. The exact allocation is complex; we focus on the outcome: total of three values.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الثاني وللحج قيمته وبه الجرح الأول، ولو كان حين أحل من العمرة قرن بحجة وعمرة ثم جرح الصيد فمات ضمن للعمرة القيمة وبه الجرح الثاني وضمن للقران قيمتين وبه الجرح الأول، ولو كان الجرح الأول استهلاكاً غرم للإحرام الأول قيمته صحيحاً وللقران قيمتين وبه الجرح الأول ا هـ . وفي مناسك الكرماني : ولو ضرب صيداً فرض وانتقصت قيمته أو ازدادت ثم مات كان عليه أكثر القيمتين من قيمته وقت الجرح أو وقت الموت .
The second: for Hajj its value, and with it the first wound. And if when he had exited from Umrah he performed qiran with Hajj and Umrah, then wounded the game and it died, he is liable for Umrah its value and with it the second wound, and liable for qiran two values and with it the first wound. And if the first wound was destruction, he pays for the first ihram its value as sound, and for qiran two values and with it the first wound. End. And in Manasik al-Kirmani: If he struck game and wounded it and its value decreased or increased then it died, upon him is the greater of the two values from its value at the time of wound or at the time of death.
Source pages p. 58

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement from the sharh of Kanz al-Daqa'iq. It addresses a scenario where a muhrim first enters ihram for Umrah, then after exiting ihram from Umrah, he enters ihram for Hajj as qiran (combining Umrah and Hajj). If he wounds game while in the second ihram (Hajj) and the game dies, the compensation is determined by the status of each ihram. The ruling distinguishes between wounds that lead to death and wounds that destroy the game entirely. If the first wound (in Umrah) was merely a wound and the game later died from the second wound (in Hajj), he must pay one value for Umrah and two values for Hajj (because qiran requires a sacrifice for each, but here it's compensation). If the first wound was actually destruction (i.e., the game died immediately from it), then he pays the full value for the first ihram and two values for qiran. The passage also cites al-Kirmani's ruling: when the value fluctuates, the maximum value between wounding and death is taken. This is a nuance not found in the basic matn but added for precision.

Key Terms
قران (qiran): A type of Hajj where Umrah and Hajj are combined with one ihram.
جرح (jarh): Wounding; in this context, any harm inflicted on game that results in compensation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a muhrim, after exiting Umrah, enters qiran for Hajj, then wounds a game in the Hajj ihram and it dies from that wound, what compensation is due?
A) One value for Umrah and two values for Hajj
B) One value for each ihram, total two
C) Two values for Hajj only
D) The maximum value between wound and death

Key Takeaway
Compensation for game in multiple ihrams depends on the sequence of wounds and whether the first wound was destructive; the Hanafi school uses a detailed allocation to ensure the penalty reflects the number of ihram violations.

Compensation for Damaging Game in Ihram: Parts and Fetuses
Explaining compensation for partial damage to game

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rulings for compensating damage to game feathers, legs, milk, eggs, and chick, and explain the legal reasoning (ta'lil) based on urdiyya, ihtiyat, and istihsan.

Core Idea
Damaging game parts requires full or proportional compensation based on their role in the game's survival or potential to become game.

This lesson delves into the detailed rulings from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq regarding compensation for partial damage to game while in the state of ihram. Understanding these rules is crucial for pilgrims to avoid sin and financial liability. We will explore the reasoning behind each ruling and the principles that guide Hanafi jurisprudence.

Guided Path
1
Identify the five acts of damage and their compensations
From the passage, list the acts: plucking feathers, cutting legs, milking, breaking eggs, and causing a dead chick. Note the compensation: full value for feathers/legs, value of milk, value of egg, and value of live chick for the last.
These compensations are wajib according to the Hanafi school.
2
Understand the ta'lil (legal reasoning) for feathers and legs
The reasoning is that removing the means of defense (feathers for flight, legs for escape) destroys the game's safety, equating to killing it. Hence full value is due.
This is a qiyas: analogy to killing the game.
3
Analyze the reasoning for milk and eggs
Milk is part of the game's body, so its value is compensatory. Eggs have potential (urdiyya) to become game, so they are treated as game by precaution (ihtiyat), supported by a narration from Ali and Ibn Abbas.
The egg ruling is based on qawl sahabi, a secondary source in Hanafi usul.
4
Distinguish between qiyas and istihsan for the dead chick
Qiyas would only require the egg's value since the chick's life is unknown. But istihsan (juristic preference) demands the value of a live chick because the egg is meant to produce a live chick, and the premature break caused death.
This shows the interplay between qiyas and istihsan in Hanafi fiqh.
5
Note exceptions and comparisons
No compensation for rotten eggs because the potentiality is absent. Also, if the chick dies from another cause, no liability. Compare with human fetus: no diyah for a dead fetus from a blow, because financial penalties are not based on precaution in human rights.
The text also discusses that roasting compensated eggs remains halal, as no slaughter is needed.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (وتجب القيمة بنتف ريشه وقطع قوائمه وحلبه وكسر بيضه وخروج فرخ ميت به أما نتف ريشه وقطع قوائمه فلأنه فوّت عليه الأمن بتفويت آلة الامتناع فصار كأنه قتله فلزمه قيمة كاملة، وأما حلبه فلأن اللبن من أجزائه فيكون معتبراً بكله فيجب عليه ضمان ما وهو قيمة اللبن، وأما كسر بيضه فلأنه أصل الصيد وله عرضية أن يصير صيداً فنزل منزلة الصيد احتياطاً وهو مروي عن علي وابن عباس رضي الله عنهما فوجب عليه قيمة البيض، وأما إذا خرج فرخ ميت بسبب الكسر فالقياس أن لا يغرم سوى قيمة البيضة لأن حياة الفرخ غير معلوم وجه الاستحسان أن البيض معد ليخرج منه الفرخ الحي والكسر قبل أوانه سبب لموته فيحال به عليه احتياطاً فتجب قيمته حياً كما صرح به. والريش جمع الريشة وهو الجناح، والقوائم الأرجل، وأطلق في كسر بيضه . وقيده في الهداية بأن لا يكون فاسداً لأنه لو كسر بيضة مذرة لا شيء عليه لأن ضمانها ليس لذاتها بل لعرضية الصيد وهو مفقود في الفاسدة، وبهذا انتفى قول الكرماني : إذا كسر بيضة نعامة مذرة وجب الجزاء لأن لقشرها قيمة، وإن كانت غيرها نعامة لا يجب شيء، وذلك لأن المحرم بالإحرام ليس منهياً عن التعرض للقشر بل للصيد فقط وليس للمذرة عرضية الصيدية كذا في فتح القدير. وفي البدائع : ولو شوى بيضاً أو جراداً فضمنه لا يحرم أكله، ولو أكله أو غيره حلالاً كان أو حراماً لا يلزمه شيء. وعلل له في المحيط بأنه لا يفتقر إلى الذكاة فلا يصير ميتة، ولهذا يباح أكل البيض قبل الشيء . وأفاد بمسألة خروج الفرخ أنه لو ضرب بطن ظبية فألقيت جنيناً ميتاً فإنه يضمن قيمته حياً، فإن ماتت الأم ضمن قيمتها أيضاً بخلاف جنين المرأة إذا خرج ميتاً لا يلزم الضارب شيئاً لأنه في حكم النفس في جزاء الصيد احتياطاً وفي حقوق العباد في حكم الجزء لأن غرامات الأموال لا تبتنى على الاحتياط كذا في النهاية. وقيد بقوله «به» لأنه لو علم موته بغير الكسر فلا ضمان عليه للفرخ لانعدام الإمانة ولا للبيض لعدم العرضية، وإذا ضمن الفرخ لا يجب في البيض شيء لأن ما ضمانه لأجله قد ضمنه. وأشار بخروج الفرخ إلى أنه لو نفر صيداً عن بيضة ففسد أنه يضمن إحالة للفساد عليه لأنه السبب الظاهر كما لو أخذ بيضة الصيد فدفنها تحت دجاجة ،ففسدت، ولو لم تفسد وخرج منها فرخ وطار فلا شيء عليه .
His saying: (And the value is obligatory for plucking its feathers, cutting its legs, milking it, breaking its egg, and the emergence of a dead chick from it. As for plucking its feathers and cutting its legs, because he has lost its safety by losing the means of resistance, so it is as if he killed it, thus a full value is obligatory. As for milking it, because the milk is part of its body, so it is considered as a whole, thus he must guarantee it, which is the value of the milk. As for breaking its egg, because it is the origin of the game and has the potential to become game; so it is treated as game as a precaution, and it is narrated from Ali and Ibn Abbas, may Allah be pleased with them, so the value of the egg is obligatory. As for when a dead chick emerges due to the break, analogically he is not liable for more than the value of the egg because the life of the chick is unknown. The basis of istihsan is that the egg is prepared for the live chick to emerge, and the break before its time is a cause of its death, so it is attributed to him as a precaution, so its value alive is obligatory as explicitly stated. And 'al-reesh' is plural of 'reesha', which is the wing, and 'al-qawa'im' are the legs. He was absolute in breaking its egg. Al-Hidayah restricted it to not being rotten, because if he broke a rotten egg, nothing is upon him, because its guarantee is not for its essence but for the potentiality of game, which is absent in the rotten. With this is refuted the statement of al-Kirmani: if he breaks a rotten ostrich egg, the penalty is obligatory because its shell has value. And if it is not an ostrich egg, nothing is obligatory. That is because the muhrim is only prohibited from harming game, not the shell, and a rotten egg has no potentiality of game. As in Fath al-Qadir. And in al-Bada'i: if one roasts eggs or locusts and then compensates for them, it is not unlawful to eat them. And if he eats them or another, whether halal or haram, nothing is obligatory upon him. And it is explained in al-Muhit that it does not require slaughter, so it does not become carrion, hence it is permissible to eat eggs before [?]. And the issue of the emergence of the chick informs that if he strikes the belly of a gazelle and she aborts a dead fetus, he is liable for its value alive; if the mother dies, he is liable for her value as well. Contrary to the human fetus: if it emerges dead, the striker is not liable for anything, because in game penalties it is treated as a soul as a precaution, but in human rights it is treated as a part because financial compensations are not based on precaution. As in al-Nihaya. And he restricted it by his saying 'by it' because if he knows its death due to other than the break, then there is no guarantee for the chick due to lack of safety, nor for the egg due to lack of potentiality. And if he guarantees the chick, nothing is due for the egg because what it was guaranteed for has been guaranteed. And by the emergence of the chick, he indicated that if he scares a game from its egg and it becomes spoiled, he is liable for the spoilage because he is the apparent cause, as if he took the game's egg and buried it under a hen and it spoils; and if it does not spoil and a chick emerges and flies away, nothing is upon him.
Source pages p. 58

Commentary
This passage is an expansion (sharh) on the matn of Kanz al-Daqa'iq regarding compensation for partial damage to game while in ihram. The commentator first defines the acts: plucking feathers, cutting legs, milking, breaking eggs, and causing a dead chick. For feathers and legs, the reasoning is that by removing the means of defense (feathers for flying, legs for escape), the muhrim has effectively rendered the game vulnerable, akin to killing it, so full value is due. For milking, the milk is considered part of the game's body, so its value must be compensated. For breaking an egg, the egg has the potential (urdiyya) to become a game, so it is treated as game by precaution (ihtiyatan). This ruling is supported by a narration (qawl sahabi) from Ali and Ibn Abbas. If the egg was rotten (mudirra), no compensation is due because the potential is absent. For a dead chick, qiyas would say only the egg's value, but istihsan (juristic preference) requires the value of a live chick because the egg is intended to produce a live chick, and the break at an improper time is the cause of death. The text also discusses roasting game parts after compensation: it remains permissible to eat because no slaughter is needed. A comparison is made with a human fetus: if a pregnant woman is struck and the fetus dies, no compensation (diyah) is due for the fetus alone because financial penalties are not based on precaution (ihtiyat) in human affairs. However, in game, the fetus is treated as a separate entity by precaution. Finally, if the chick's death is known from another cause, no compensation; and if the egg is taken and hatches successfully, no liability.

Key Terms
عرضية (urdiyya): Potentiality or incidental quality; the egg's potential to become a game.
احتياط (ihtiyat): Precaution; a basis for istihsan in some rulings, especially in ibadat and penalties.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Qiyas on killing an adult game
B) Qawl sahabi from Ali and Ibn Abbas
C) Istihsan because the egg is meant to produce a live chick
D) The egg's intrinsic value

Key Takeaway
Compensation for game parts in ihram hinges on the potential (urdiyya) and precaution (ihtiyat), with istihsan overriding strict analogy in the case of a dead chick.
